Imagine…

 

ACTORS:

Narrator:

Dad (James): 

Mom (Cynthia):

Child 1 (Tammy):

Child 2 (Lisa):

Child 3 (Kyle)

Doctor

Nurse 1

Nurse 2

 

EXTRAS:

Light Person: ____________________________________

Radio 1 (Carl): Pre-recording or _____________________

Radio 2 (Brenda): Pre-recording or ___________________

President: Pre-recording or __________________________

 

SKIT:

 

NARRATOR:  Imagine that the day is over and you’ve just arrived home.  You tune in your radio and you hear the following news:

 

Scene 1

Dad arrives home, empties his pockets on the side table and turns on the radio.

DAD:  Honey, I’m home.

MOM:  I’m in the kitchen!  I’ll be right there!

All three kids are on the dining room table)

CHILD 1:  Hey, Dad!  Guess what I got on my geometry test.

CHILD 2:  No, you gotta come and look at my project first, I did great!

CHILD 3:  (Gets up and kisses his Dad then shows him his paper)  Hi Dad!

DAD:  (Checking out Kyle’s work) Wow, Kyle, you did great!  I’m so proud of you.

CHILD 1 and 2:  (Twists their mouths, look at each other and start making fun of Kyle)

MOM:  Stop that, girls!

 

Music stops from the radio and the following news comes through.

RADIO 1: And now, some news from around the world: “In India, it’s been reported that several villagers have died suddenly and strangely, from a flu that has never been seen before.

 

NARRATOR:  You don’t think much about it.  However, the next day after coming home from church, you hear another radio spot.

 

Scene 2:

Everyone arrives home from church service.  Dad turns on the radio and background music is heard.

MOM:  What a wonderful service!

DAD:  I know.  Pastor Charles has been such a blessing to our family.  It’s amazing how the Lord uses him.  Did you see that lady and her daughter when they stood up and gave their lives to the Lord?  It was so touching to see both of them making that decision together!

MOM:  I agree.  It reminded me of the time when I asked the Lord into my life.  I cried during the entire service.  I felt like I had finally found what I’d been missing for so long!  (Looking at the children)  Okay kids, it’s time for bed.  You have school tomorrow.

CHILD 1:  Aww!  It’s only ten o’clock…

CHILD 2:  Yeah!

CHILD 1:  We haven’t even had our snacks yet!

CHILD 2:  Yeah!

CHILD 3:  I’m hungry.

CHILD 2:  Yeah!

 

MOM:  (Laughingly) Lisa, you really don’t need to agree with everything Tammy and Kyle says.  Besides with all the snacks you had at church, I think you’ve already had your entire week’s worth of snacks covered!   And didn’t we just eat at Riley’s?  Sheesh!  Dad’s going to have to get another job just to feed you guys!  (Looking lovingly, mom pauses then) Okay, go get ready for bed and I’ll prepare some fruit cups.

 

CHILD 1,2 & 3:  Yeah!  (Children run off)

RADIO 2:  This just in:  The flu in India has already claimed the lives of 30,000 villagers in the back hills of the Northeast area of the town of Nabul.  Scientists from the Center of Disease Control in Atlanta are headed to India tonight.  This strain has never been seen before and has many doctors scratching their heads.

 

NARRATOR:

By Monday morning it’s the lead story in the television.  You see, now the disease has spread to other countries.

 

Scene 3:

Everyone is sitting at the dinning room table enjoying their supper while the radio plays music in the background.

MOM:  Honey, can you pass me the milk.

CHILD 1:  Mom, Lisa has a crush on Michael.  I heard her telling Nancy at PE today.

CHILD 2:  Do not!

CHILD 1:  Do too!

CHILD 2:  Do not!  Mom, Tammy’s bugging me!  Tell her to stop!

CHILD 1:  Stop whining.  What do you think Michael’s going to think?

CHILD 2:  MOM!

CHILD 3:  (Laughs shaking his head and rolls his eyes)

DAD:  Girls, be quiet!  (Raises his index finger in a listening mode)

 

RADIO 1:  The disease has now spread to Pakistan, Afghanistan and China.  France announced the closing of their border this past Monday, but we are afraid that it’s already too late for them.  Several people have already begun to show symptoms of the disease.  It seems that this disease has already reached Europe!

RADIO 2:  Carl, can you tell us what the symptoms are?

MOM:  (Mom goes behind dad and puts her hands on his shoulders.  Dad pats her hand.)  

RADIO 1:  It seems that they’re not too sure, but from what we’ve heard, once you get it, you have it for a week before you know it.  Then you have four days of unbelievable symptoms, and then you die!

RADIO 2:  Oh my!  Do they kno…

RADIO 1:  Hold on Brenda.  Ladies and Gentlemen, the President of the United States.  (Pause)

PRESIDENT:  My fellow Americans, I just got off the phone with Britain.  In an attempt to help control this disease, they have informed me that they have closed their borders this morning, but it seems that it’s too late.  I’ve been informed that the disease has already spread to South Hampton, Liverpool and North Hampton.  (pause & sigh)  I regret to say, that due to a national security risk, all flights to and from Europe and Asia have been canceled.  If your loved ones are over seas, I’m sorry (pause), they will not be allowed to come back until we find a cure for this disease.

(Mom and dad look at each other, mom puts her hand on her mouth)

 

NARRATOR:

Within four days our nation has been plunged into an unbelievable fear.  Can you imagine?  People are selling little face masks.  You can hear people asking, “What if it comes to America?”  Preachers are yelling, “It’s the wrath of God!”  But what they didn’t know is that it had already reached American soil.  For one night while mom and dad were reading the Bible, dad received a phone call from his mother.

 

Scene 4:

(Phone rings, mom gets it)

MOM:  Oh, Hi.  How’s everything going?  Sure, he’s right here.  Hold on a second. (mom covers the phone and faces dad)  Honey, it’s your mom.

DAD:  Thanks.  Hi mom. (pause) Uh-huh.  Okay, I’ll do it right now.  (Dad walks to the radio)

MOM:  You know James, I was thinking…(Dad lifts his finger in an act of telling her to listen)

RADIO 1:  (With a solemn voice)  We regret to inform you that this fateful disease has reached the United States.  Two women are lying in a Long Island hospital dying from this mysterious flu. 

(Mom and dad look at each other with concern)

 

NARRATOR:  Within hours it seems that this thing is just sweeping across the United States!  Scientists are working around the clock trying to find an antidote, but nothing works!  California, Arizona, Oregon, even Florida!  It’s as though it’s sweeping the entire nation!  Then all of a sudden, there’s some “good news”.

 

Scene 5:

Dad, with garden gloves, enters the house very excitedly.  Goes to the table and puts on the radio. Both of them have the sniffles and an all around “ill” appearance.

MOM:  James, what’s wrong?

DAD:  The code has been broken.

MOM:  What are you talking about?  The virus?

DAD:  Yeah!  They found a cure!  Scientists can now make a vaccine.  They’re going to start driving through the neighborhoods in a couple of hours, and when we hear the sirens go off, we need to go down to the hospital and have our blood drawn.

MOM:  How about the kids?

DAD:  Everyone!  They need to check us all!  They’re looking for a certain type of blood, from someone who hasn’t been infected.  (sniffles) Everyone’s talking about it!  Come on, let’s get ready.

MOM:  Okay.  I’ll go get them.

 

NARRATOR:  Sure enough, you hear the siren, and when you and your family get down to the hospital, there is a long line.  They’ve got doctors and nurses coming out and pricking everyone’s fingers, taking blood and putting labels on it.  Your wife and your kids are right there with you.

 

Scene 6:

NURSE 1:  (Pricks the fingers of the family.  Tammy and Lisa complain)

NURSE 2:  (With a clipboard)  Wait here in the parking lot and if we call your name, you can be dismissed and go home.

Mom places her head in her hands and dad tries to comfort her.

DOCTOR:  (All excitedly, with the clipboard on his hand)  Kyle Peterson, Kyle Peterson!!!

CHILD 3:  Dad, that’s me!

The doctor motions for Kyle to follow him and both start to leave.  

DAD:  Hey, wait a minute!  What’s going on?

DOCTOR 1:  It’s okay, his blood is clean, it’s pure.  We just want to make sure that he doesn’t have the disease.  We think he has the right type of blood.

After a couple of seconds, the doctor comes out.

DOCTOR 1:  Your son’s blood type is perfect.  It’s clean, it’s pure.  We can make the vaccine!

 

NARRATOR:  The doctors and nurses are crying and hugging one another, some are even laughing.  It’s the first time you’ve seen anybody laugh in a week.  As the word begins to spread all across the parking lot, you see people dancing, laughing, praying and crying.  Then all of a sudden, the doctor approaches you with a solemn voice.

 

Doctor calls dad aside and both begin to walk towards the hospital.

DOCTOR 2:  We didn’t know that the donor would be a minor, so we need you to sign a consent form.

Doctor shows dad the form and dad proceeds to sign, but he stops.

DAD:  H-how many pints of blood do you need?  It doesn’t specify.

DOCTOR 2:  We had no idea it would be a young child.  We weren’t prepared…..We need it all!

DAD:  But, but….

DOCTOR 2:  You don’t understand.  We are talking about the world here.  Please sign.  

DAD:  I can’t do this.  How do you expect me to allow you to kill my own son? 

DOCTOR 2:  Sir, if we need to call the authorities to approve this, we will.  Please understand!  I know how difficult this is for you, but the world is dying!

DAD:  But can’t you give him a transfusion?

DOCTOR 2:  If we had clean blood we would.  Can you, please?

In numb silence dad signs the paper.

DOCTOR 2:  Would you like to have a moment with him before we begin?

 

Scene 7:

Dad walks up to his son who is sitting on a table.

CHILD 3:  Hey Dad.  (Flexing his muscles and smiling)  Looks like I’m going to be the hero here, eh?  You can start calling me Superman!  (All of a sudden he notices his dad’s concerned look)  What’s going on?  

DAD:  Son, you know that I love you and I wouldn’t let anything happen to you that didn’t have to be.  Do you understand that?

CHILD 3:  (With a concerned look)  Sure, Dad???

DOCTOR:  (Walking back into the room)  I’m very sorry, we’ve got to get started.  People all over the world are dying.

 

NARRATOR:  (Standing up and taking the middle of the stage)  Can you leave?  Can you walk back in that room while he is saying, “Father, Father?  Why have you forsaken me?   Can you allow your son to give up his life so that others can live?  Thieves, murderers, drug addicts…

 

Well, somebody has already done that, and His name is Jesus Christ.  Jesus came to this world and gave His life so that those who believe in Him can live an everlasting life.

 

Let’s bow down our heads and thank God for His awesome love.  And if you haven’t met the Lord, I encourage you to ask Him to come into your life while we pray.  All you have to do is ask for forgiveness and invite Him into your life!

 

Let’s pray.  Father, seeing it from Your eyes breaks our hearts.  Maybe now we can comprehend the great love that you have for us.  Please continue to love us and guide us in your ways.  Do not let us wander.  And Father, if there is someone who hasn’t met you here today, I ask that you touch that person with your Holy Spirit.  Thank you Lord for always loving us.  Amen.

 

MOM:  (Walking to the left of NARRATOR as if reading the Bible) For God so loved us that He gave His only begotten Son so that we could be saved…

DAD:  (Walking to the right of NARRATOR) Thank you for joining us today.  May God Bless all of you!

 

Music plays “I can only Imagine” by Mercy Me

Everyone moves to the front and takes a bow…

 

Running time:  Approximately 25 Minutes

My primary reason for wishing to change my status from U.S. Citizen to illegal alien stem from the bill which was recently passed by the Senate. If my understanding of this bill's provisions is accurate, as an illegal alien who has been in the United States for five years, all I need to do to become a citizen is to pay a $2,000 fine and income taxes for three of the last five years. I know a good deal when I see one and I am anxious to get the process started before everyone figures it out. 
Simply put, those of us who have been here legally have had to pay taxes every year so I'm excited about the prospect of avoiding two years of taxes in return for paying a $2,000 fine. Is there any way that I can apply to be illegal retroactively? This would yield an excellent result for me and my family because we paid heavy taxes in 2004 and 2005. 
Additionally, as an illegal alien I could begin using the local emergency room as my primary health care provider. Once I have stopped paying premiums for medical insurance, my accountant figures I could save almost $10,000 a year. Lastly, I understand that illegal status would relieve me of the burden of renewing my driver's license and making those burdensome car insurance premiums. This is very important to me given that I still have college age children driving my car. 
If you would provide me with an outline of the process to become illegal (retroactively if possible) and copies of the necessary forms, I would be most appreciative. Thank you for your assistance. 
Your Loyal Constituent,

> > When does Medicare coverage start? < <

If you enro~l while still covered by a GHP based on current employment or before the end of the first full month following the end of coverage/employment, your Medicare coverage begins with your

	the month you enrolled, or

	any of the 3 months following the month yau enrolled.

Lauren Miller

Dear Governor Bush:

Please Support
Access to Physical Medicine and Rehabilitation Services Improvement Act 
(S.3963)

I am an ATHLETIC TRAINING student.  Athletic trainers are health care 
professionals educated and trained in the prevention, assessment, 
treatment and rehabilitation of injuries and illnesses. There are almost 
7,400 athletic training students and a total of 30,000 certified athletic 
trainers working in high schools, colleges, hospitals, clinics and 
academia. Athletic trainers in the U.S. treat an estimated 16 million 
patients each year and are an essential part of the health care system.

The ability of athletic trainers to provide care has been impeded by an 
unfair policy rule made by the Center for Medicare and Medicaid Services 
(CMS) in July 2005. This "incident to" ruling restricts health care 
providers from referring their patients to athletic trainers, lymphedema 
therapists, and others. This drastically limits a patient's ability to 
choose who they see for medical treatment. By cosponsoring S.3963, the 
Access to Physical Medicine and Rehabilitation Services Improvement Act, 
and pressing for its speedy vote and passage, you can help to improve 
access to quality health care services provided by athletic trainers and 
other therapists for Medicare beneficiaries.  It will also restore the 
ability of physicians to choose who can help them deliver these services 
in their office.  

Athletic trainers work under a physician's direction in providing 
medically necessary health care services. This bill lifts artificial and 
arbitrary restrictions on athletic trainers as health care professionals 
and allows athletic trainers to treat all patients within their scope of 
practice.  All athletic trainers hold bachelor's degrees and 70 percent 
have master's or doctoral degrees.  All certified athletic trainers must 
pass a national board exam to become certified.

Please cosponsor S.3963.  Join athletic trainers in our fight to keep the 
quality of health care high by empowering our patients and physicians to 
have freedom in their medical care options.  

Sincerely,


Lauren Miller
813-323-0015

From:	MD and Tracy G. Sanson Kelly P. O'Keefe <oaks61596@aol.com>

MD and Tracy G. Sanson Kelly P. O'Keefe

Dear Governor Bush:

Dear Sir,

   We are emergency physicians in Florida.  I am the medical director of 
the adult emergency department at Tampa General Hospital, the trauma 
center for the Tampa area.  I am also the residency director for the 
emergency medicine residency program.  My wife is also an emergency 
physician at Tampa General and education director for the University of 
South Florida emergency medicine program and medical students. In our work 
at Tampa General Hospital and for the University of South Florida, we are 
at the forefront of our patient's medical needs and intimately involved in 
the education of the students and physicians who will care for them in the 
future.  We are affiliated with TeamHealth. TeamHealth is one of the 
largest physician organizations in the United States and 
TeamHealth-affiliated physicians will treat over 1,200,000 Medicare 
patients in 2006.TeamHealth serves 470 hospitals and clinics in 44 states 
and contracts with over 5,000 emergency department physicians, physician 
assistants and nurse practitioners.  The work of these clinicians is 
supported by over 2,000 administrative employees across the United States. 
  My colleagues and I are all extremely concerned with the scheduled 
Medicare physician payment reductions in 2006 and beyond. In fact, a 5.1% 
reduction in the Medicare fee schedule will reduce payments to emergency 
room physicians by over $6.00 per patient encounter.  Like any other 
business subject to increased costs of doing business and inflation, we 
cannot withstand continued reductions in our practice revenues.

   Emergency physicians provide care to millions of uninsured patients 
each year. Much of this care is uncompensated. In addition, we care for 
millions of Medicaid patients, due in many cases to these patients' lack 
of access to appropriate care from both primary and specialty care 
physicians. The Medicare payments we receive support what has increasingly 
become a very fragile safety net.  

   TeamHealth and its physicians have worked for many years with the 
Emergency Department Practice Management Association (EDPMA) and the 
American College of Emergency Physicians (ACEP) in support of emergency 
medicine. The Institute of Medicine (IOM) recently published a series of 
reports on the state of emergency care in our nation, and they paint a 
grim picture. The IOM has urged Congress that "the emergency care system 
requires a special funding source, separate from the regular DSH formula, 
to adequately compensate hospitals and physicians for the burden of 
providing services to uninsured and underinsured populations."

   In the absence of Congressional or Executive action, Medicare payment 
rates for all physicians will fall by approximately 5.1% in January of 
2007. This is due to a "flawed" formula within the Medicare physician 
payment system. Resolution of this issue needs to occur during the 
upcoming Lame Duck Session of Congress.  I urge you to take action by 
passing legislation that will avert this reduction in 2007 and find a long 
term solution to the Sustainable Growth Rate formula dilemma.

   Emergency physicians work every day to improve the quality of care 
delivered in our communities.  As part of that effort, TeamHealth has an 
established dialogue with the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services 
(CMS) in order to participate in pay-for-performance (P4P) initiatives and 
has begun to submit P4P data to CMS this year. We are extremely interested 
in continuing to work with CMS and Congress to improve patient care. I 
invite you to visit one of our emergency departments as your schedule 
permits so that we can show you just what kind of vital work our 
physicians are doing in your community.

   Thank you for your consideration.

Sincerely,

Kelly P. O'Keefe MD, FACEP
Medical Director Adult Emergency Department Tampa General Hospital
Residency Director University of South Florida Emergency Medicine 
Residency Program

Tracy G. Sanson MD, FACEP
Education Director  University of South Florida Emergency Medicine 
Residency Program and Medical Student Clerkship


Sincerely,


MD and Tracy G. Sanson Kelly P. O'Keefe
813-948-6190

 Governor Bush:

I write to you today concerning a matter that is of grave importance to my 
family, loved ones and to myself.  On June 21, 2005, Senator Leahy (D-VT) 
and Congressman Nadler (D-NY) introduced the Uniting American Families Act 
into the U.S. Congress.  The Uniting American Families Act seeks to amend 
the Immigration and Nationality Act by adding the term "permanent partner" 
where the word spouse appears thus allowing gay and lesbian U.S. citizens 
the opportunity to sponsor their partners for immigration to the U.S.    

U.S. immigration law is based on the principle of family unification.

petitions.  The fact that gay and lesbian U.S. citizens cannot sponsor 
their same-sex partners is grossly unjust and contradicts the policy of 
promoting family unification.  I would like to have the opportunity to

quality of my relationship of over [X] years with my partner, who is a 
citizen of [name of country].  [insert personal story here]

convenience to arrange an appointment.  Thank you very much for your time 
in this important matter.

Thats when things began going downhill.  I was contacted by FEMA and was told that I was ineligable for personal property assistance because the housing inspector told them I had insufficient damage.  I explained to them that wasnt possible because my apartment was condemned.  How can I have insufficient damage when my apartment is so bad that I can barely walk in it?  I mean my ceiling had become my floor.  So I appealled the decision and was told that an inspector would be calling me.  Now while this is going on I am calling every week to keep up on the status of my appeall.  Well on August 8, 2006 I was notified once again that I had unsufficient losses.  And once again neither I nor the management office for the apartment I stayed in heard word one from FEMA.  So to this day I havent received 1 penny for personal property assistance.

I received a payment of $1776 to assist with my rental payments for the months of Nov, Dec & Jan.  I submitted my paperwork in April for Feb, Mar and April. I had to find a way to pay the rent so I left my wife (who started school in December and could not leave) and my 4 year old son and left to stay with a friend in Orlando so I could find a decent job.  
 
In June I became 2 months late with rent and my family was facing eviction because FEMA denied me what was promised to cover 18 months.  I managed to borrow enough money from people to catch up on rent but knew that I know owe friends and that if FEMA denied me again I would be evicted.  
 
So after months of the runaround with FEMA in July I was finally told to supply certain paperwork and I would be given backpay for Feb - Apr plus my assistance for May - July.  I submitted the exact same paperwork I submitted in April plus my new receipts and was approved.  I received $1782 on July 27 to cover May - Jul but did not receive the backpay.  By this time I was extremely tired of calling FEMA and getting nothing so I gave up on the backpay and hoped that when it came time for my next payment that everything would go through fine.  Of course that didn't happen.  When I submitted my paperwork to cover Aug - Oct I was denied yet again.  
 
This time the reasons beat all the others.  All of the paperwork that was good before somehow became invalid.  I spoke to a supervisor over the housing assistance program who gave me multiple reasons why my assistance was denied.  1)  They have no record of where I lived prior to the hurricane  2)  The lease that they have had on file from day 1 has somehow become inelibible because now it looks like I am the one that wrote it 3)  My rent receipts are invalid because 2 of them say I payed in September which is true because I was late because FEMA wouldnt help me and 4)  That my landlords business number which is also his personal cell phone cannot be a real number because the voicemail picks up "Hello" and according to the lady I spoke with NO business has a voicemail like that.  And of course when I tried to dispute these, I was told that if I didnt correct them then I would not receive assistance.

From:	Bill_J <mikeybird723@earthlink.net>
Sent:	Tuesday, December 5, 2006 1:12 PM
To:	vice.president@whitehouse.gov; president@whitehouse.gov; Governor Jeb Bush
Subject:	ASKING YOUR HELP

William Jenkins

116A N. College St.

Leesburg, FL 34748

Tel. 352-326-3032

 

December 5, 2006

 

To Whom It May Concern:

 

I was recently made aware that Medicare will only provide powered wheelchairs which suit the person’s needs inside his/her home.  I am a double amputee quadriplegic and use a powered wheelchair.  To say that this mandate appalls me is an understatement.  Most powered wheelchairs that are only suited for indoor use are next to useless outside of the home.  Since going outside at some times is a necessary activity, doing so in an underpowered chair only suited for indoor use would be dangerous, it might end up costing Medicare far more money due to accidents caused by unsafe use of such wheelchairs.  Not to mention possible lawsuits that would eventually be filed.  Then there are the thousands of jobs that could be lost because wheelchair manufacturers and distributors would be put out of business, resulting in lost tax revenue and higher unemployment expenses.

 

Does Medicare really want disabled people to stay inside all of the time?  Isn’t that discrimination against people with disabilities and, therefore, in violation of the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA)?  Are we not allowed to venture outside for doctor appointments (something required to remain living in many cases), grocery shopping (another activity necessary to live), or just to enjoy going outside for a social activity (a vital activity for our mental health)?  Are we to be condemned to a life inside our homes as if we were hermits?

 

Back in the 1980’s, I was on several committees at my college that help write the ADA and was proud to have been asked to participate in drafting that landmark legislation.  I had no idea that in the future the federal government would be the entity that violated that act.  It is unconscionable that a government agency that provides healthcare availability to the disabled would attempt to so blatantly violate an act of Congress.

 

I’m requesting that this extreme restriction on the type of powered wheelchairs we can obtain through Medicare be changed.  Being disabled and on Medicare should not mean we are relegated to being “out of sight, out of mind” as it seems this agency (Medicare) desires.  I am only 56 years old and am not going to stay indoors the remainder of my life.  This “wheelchair edict,” as I call it, is far too limiting and needs to be changed.  That change needs to be made as soon as humanly possible.

 

This is of utmost importance as it affects both the physical and mental health of all persons needing powered wheelchairs.  Please allow our doctors, Physical Therapists, Occupational Therapists and wheelchair seating specialists determine which wheelchairs best suit our needs as far as comfort, power, safety and health are concerned.  Don’t leave our ability to be mobile, safe and comfortable in the hands of a Medicare or Medicaid bureaucrat.  People with disabilities struggle with many things.  Don’t make them struggle to just move around.

 

 

Respectfully,

William Jenkins

Getting experienced people to move to the Treasure Coast where there was no HMO was not easy. We were busy opening Primary Care Centers to take care of members and our Centers were the 1st Centers that gave the member hr right to come to the office any time, 7 days a week, with no Co pays for the Primary Care or Specialist visit. Our benefits were the best in any County. 
 
In  Nov. 2002 we expanded to Palm Beach and no HMO gave the benefits we gave. In Nov. 2003 we expanded to Broward county and our benefits were richer then Humana , Care plus or Well Care. We beat the competition hands down. In Sept. of 2004 we were hit 3 times by all the hurricanes that hit the Treasure Coast. Our Corporate Office and staff were affected 3 times. We were visited by CMS in January and we had not fixed the deficiencies they wanted fixed. They did not even consider that our medical centers and main office were all affected. We had construction, staffing, relocation and all the various problems that only a large recurring hurricane could damage. When I mentioned it to our Plan manager at CMS and asked her for a stay or an extension she said all HMOs had been affected . Who were we to challenge her.? So they came . Neither the staff not the problems could get fixed when peoples homes were destroyed, they had mold in their homes and needed time to take care of themselves.
 
We made many changes to be in compliance and when we saw that CMS was not being responsive to any thing that we did we decided to sell the Company and get out of the HMO industry and keep the medical centers that gave the care to the members. The sale did not go through. At the 11th  hour the public Company that was to buy us and had been managing us for 8 months with drew their offer. They changed their minds and wanted to pick us up for nothing as CMS kept telling us to close the deal or they would put sanctions. HealthSpring did not want to pay us even a 1/3 of the original selling price and expected us to acquiesce . We did not. They are still managing us and making $800,000 per month doing this with 2 employees from Nashville who commute to Vero Beach.

*	 13,000 seniors , will be asked to disenroll from America's Health Choice.  
*	Some of these areas have only 1 HMO. 
*	Members will not have the choice of seeing the doctors they saw for 5 years. In 4 counties AHCMP has between 85% to 97 % of Medicare HMO membership. 
*	 Just before Christmas about 150 employees of America's Health Choice will be let go. 
*	 An additional 100 employees will be released from the Medical Centers when membership changes. 
*	 America's Health Choice did do all that was required in the Corrective Action Plan and yet CMS refuses to accept them since 2005. 
*	America's Health Choice Medical Plans and its employees request you to intervene on their behalf to stop the termination from occurring. 
*	AHCMP has presented a Temporary Restraining Order and an injunction on Saturday to have the Courts review the merits of the termination decision. 
*	We were there for the community for 5 years when there were no HMO in these rural and semi rural areas. Now that reimbursements are high and CMS has choices they have chosen to  abuse their power and make us, a small Company an example . CMS has kept us under unfair scrutiny since 2005. of Currently all the compliance issues have been rectified. We are not only well with in the days to pay electronic claims and process appeals and grievances but we are above the industry average. 
*	When sanctions were placed and enrollments in the plan stopped we were 16,000 members and a year and a half later we have managed to keep 13,000 members. Can it be in spite of the normal rate of attrition after the hurricanes and the normal death and relocation of residences and no new members added to the plan we would have had all those members if the medical care and service was not good.?  
*

No consideration was given for the devastation of the 3 hurricanes that hit our home base and the residences of our employees. Governor Jeb Bush <jeb.bush@myflorida.com> wrote: 

For those E-Newsletter recipients who have Adobe Acrobat reader, Governor
Bush's e-newsletter is available in .PDF format by clicking here:

http://www.flgov.com/in_the_news

The text version of the e-newsletter is below.


CECIL FIELD COMMERCE CENTER SELECTED AS SITE FOR MAJOR AVIATION PRODUCTION
SITE

On Monday, I applauded the C-27J industry team of L-3 Communications
Integrated Systems, Finmeccanica's Alenia North America, Global Military
Aircraft Systems and Boeing Integrated Defense Systems for their commitment
to establish the group's advanced aircraft operation at Jacksonville's Cecil
Commerce Center if awarded a Department of Defense contract. I toured the
C-27J aircraft and potential assembly and production site along with
Congressman Ander Crenshaw, Jacksonville Mayor John Peyton, and state and
local business leaders. In selecting Jacksonville's Cecil Field, the C-27J
Joint Cargo Aircraft team has embraced the strengths of our state's
pro-business climate, robust defense industry and highly skilled aviation
and aerospace workforce. This new assembly and production activity will
enhance Florida' economy and would be a great addition to the state's
thriving aviation sector, currently the third strongest in the nation. Most
importantly, the C-27J will help our men and women of the Army and the Air
Force continue to serve and defend our country. The Department of Defense
is expected to award the Joint Cargo Aircraft contract in early 2007. Should
the Department award the multi-billion dollar contract to the C-27J team,
the group will begin establishing its advanced aircraft operation at the
Jacksonville site in 2007. The facility is expected to employ more than 200
people. For more information on our economic development initiatives,
please visit www.myflorida.com.


2006 FLORIDA YOUTH SUBSTANCE ABUSE SURVEY RESULTS ANNOUNCED

On Tuesday, I announced the results of the 2006 Florida Youth Substance
Abuse Survey. In the last eight years, we have worked to strengthen
substance abuse prevention, and we have seen significant progress in the
cause. This year's results confirm that progress is being made, but the
work is not done. Since 2000, Florida has seen declines in the use of
heroin, ecstasy and LSD, as well as in the use of cigarettes and alcohol.
This year, 12 of the 21 categories measured current use below two percent.
Conducted among 6th through 12th graders throughout the state for the
seventh consecutive year, the Florida Youth Substance Abuse Survey is the
most extensive survey of its kind in the nation. The survey assesses
lifetime drug usage and current usage. I was joined for Tuesday's
announcement by First Lady Columba Bush, Lt. Governor Toni Jennings,
Director of the Florida Office of Drug Control Bill Janes, state agency
heads, law enforcement officials and substance abuse prevention specialists
- key partners in reducing substance abuse throughout the state. For view
the complete results of the 2006 Florida Youth Substance Abuse Survey,
please visit www.dcf.state.fl.us/mentalhealth/publications/fysas.


2006 FLORIDA HOLIDAY ORNAMENT AND GOVERNOR'S MANSION 50TH ANNIVERSARY
COMMEMORATIVE BOOK AVAILABLE

The Florida Governor's Mansion Foundation is pleased to announce its annual
holiday ornament, the fourth in a series. Coinciding with its 50th
anniversary and inclusion in the National Register of Historic Places, the
image of the Governor's Mansion is appropriately featured on this year's
ornament. The Foundation is also proud to announce the publication of First
Families in Residence: Life at the Florida Governor's Mansion, by
distinguished architectural historian Ellen J. Uguccioni. The new
commemorative book is a lively chronicle of both the residence and the lives
of the families, including interviews with many governors, first ladies and
family members, as well as outstanding new and archival photographs never
before published. To view and order both the new 2006 ornament (as well as
2003, 2004, & 2005 ornaments) and the book, please visit:
www.floridashistoryshop.com or call (850) 245-6396.


POINTS OF LIGHT AWARDED TO GREGG SPEERS

Congratulations!

To read more about this week's winner, please click here: 
http://www.flgov.com/release/8424

local business leaders.  In selecting Jacksonville's Cecil Field, the C-27J
Joint Cargo Aircraft team has embraced the strengths of our state's
pro-business climate, robust defense industry and highly skilled aviation
and aerospace workforce.  This new assembly and production activity will
enhance Florida' economy and would be a great addition to the state's
thriving aviation sector, currently the third strongest in the nation. Most
importantly, the C-27J will help our men and women of the Army and the Air
Force continue to serve and defend our country.  The Department of Defense
is expected to award the Joint Cargo Aircraft contract in early 2007. Should
the Department award the multi-billion dollar contract to the C-27J team,
the group will begin establishing its advanced aircraft operation at the
Jacksonville site in 2007. The facility is expected to employ more than 200
people.  For more information on our economic development initiatives,
please visit www.myflorida.com.


2006 FLORIDA YOUTH SUBSTANCE ABUSE SURVEY RESULTS ANNOUNCED

On Tuesday, I announced the results of the 2006 Florida Youth Substance
Abuse Survey. In the last eight years, we have worked to strengthen
substance abuse prevention, and we have seen significant progress in the
cause.  This year's results confirm that progress is being made, but the
work is not done.  Since 2000, Florida has seen declines in the use of
heroin, ecstasy and LSD, as well as in the use of cigarettes and alcohol.
This year, 12 of the 21 categories measured current use below two percent.
Conducted among 6th through 12th graders throughout the state for the
seventh consecutive year, the Florida Youth Substance Abuse Survey is the
most extensive survey of its kind in the nation.  The survey assesses
lifetime drug usage and current usage.   I was joined for Tuesday's
announcement by First Lady Columba Bush, Lt. Governor Toni Jennings,
Director of the Florida Office of Drug Control Bill Janes, state agency
heads, law enforcement officials and substance abuse prevention specialists
- key partners in reducing substance abuse throughout the state. For view
the complete results of the 2006 Florida Youth Substance Abuse Survey,
please visit www.dcf.state.fl.us/mentalhealth/publications/fysas.
      

2006 FLORIDA HOLIDAY ORNAMENT AND GOVERNOR'S MANSION 50TH ANNIVERSARY
COMMEMORATIVE BOOK AVAILABLE

The Florida Governor's Mansion Foundation is pleased to announce its annual
holiday ornament, the fourth in a series.  Coinciding with its 50th
anniversary and inclusion in the National Register of Historic Places, the
image of the Governor's Mansion is appropriately featured on this year's
ornament. The Foundation is also proud to announce the publication of First
Families in Residence: Life at the Florida Governor's Mansion, by
distinguished architectural historian Ellen J. Uguccioni. The new
commemorative book is a lively chronicle of both the residence and the lives
of the families, including interviews with many governors, first ladies and
family members, as well as outstanding new and archival photographs never
before published. To view and order both the new 2006 ornament (as well as
2003, 2004, & 2005 ornaments) and the book, please visit:
www.floridashistoryshop.com or call (850) 245-6396.

From:	Carolina Romero <kikarra_2000@yahoo.es>
Sent:	Tuesday, November 28, 2006 3:00 PM
To:	Governor Jeb Bush
Subject:	Mohammad Hanif Atta Mohammad, de 37 años, ciudadano pakistaní, Jasmine Anwar Hussain, de 23, ciudadana bangladeshí, Mohammad Hilaluddin, de 33, ciudadano bangladeshí

Señora Secretaria de Estado Rice,
Siento una honda preocupación por el uso de centros de detención secreta –también conocidos como “lugares negros”– que facilitan una política de “desapariciones”, traslados secretos y detenciones secretas en régimen de incomunicación por parte del gobierno estadounidense en el contexto de su “guerra contra el terror”.
El caso de Muhammad Abdullah Salah al-Assad ilustra esta cuestión. Muhammad al-Assad, ciudadano yemení residente en Tanzania, fue detenido por las autoridades tanzanas en diciembre de 2003. Los informes indican que fue entregado a agentes estadounidenses e interrogado en una serie de centros de detención secreta en el extranjero. Permaneció 16 meses recluido en régimen de incomunicación. El trato que ha descrito en el último centro corrobora los testimonios dados a Amnistía Internacional por Salah Nasser Salim ‘Ali y Muhammad Faraj Ahmed Bashmillah sobre su detención en un centro encubierto gestionado por Estados Unidos. Los tres hombres fueron trasladados a Yemen en mayo de 2005, y allí permanecen detenidos sin cargos ni juicio.
Las autoridades yemeníes han dicho a Amnistía Internacional que la Embajada estadounidense en Saná les notificó el traslado de los tres hombres a Yemen y les dio instrucciones específicas de que no los pusieran en libertad. Las autoridades yemeníes afirman estar “a la espera de recibir expedientes” de Estados Unidos para poder someter a los tres hombres a juicio. Un alto cargo de los servicios de seguridad política de Yemen ha declarado que los tres serían liberados si el gobierno estadounidense lo pidiera.
La “guerra contra el terror” emprendida por Estados Unidos se ha caracterizado por el secreto, desde la práctica de ocultar a los detenidos en Afganistán e Irak, pasando por las “entregas extraordinarias”, hasta llegar a la negativa de Estados Unidos a proporcionar datos exactos sobre quiénes se encuentran detenidos en la bahía de Guantánamo. El uso de estos “lugares negros” para facilitar la detención indefinida y en régimen de incomunicación de sospechosos es sólo el ejemplo más reciente de estas políticas.
Señora Secretaria, le insto a:
- desvelar el lugar y la categoría de los centros de detención en los que estuvieron recluidos Muhammad Abdullah Salah al-Assad, Muhammad Faraj Ahmed Bashmilah y Salah Nasser Salim ‘Ali; le insto también a desvelar la identidad y el paradero de todas las demás personas recluidas en este centro, así como su situación legal, y a invitar al Comité Internacional de la Cruz Roja a acceder de forma completa y periódica a estas personas;
- poner fin de inmediato a la práctica de la detención secreta y en régimen de incomunicación donde quiera que tenga lugar y sea cual sea la agencia responsable de ella;
- recluir a las personas detenidas únicamente en lugares de detención oficialmente reconocidos, con acceso a familiares, abogados y tribunales;
- garantizar que toda persona que sea presuntamente responsable de un acto de “desaparición” comparezca, cuando los hechos desvelados por una investigación oficial así lo justifiquen, ante las autoridades civiles competentes para ser acusada y juzgada, de acuerdo con el artículo 14 de la Declaración de las Naciones Unidas sobre la Protección de Todas las Personas contra las Desapariciones Forzadas;
- aclarar la situación legal actual de Muhammad Abdullah Salah al-Assad, Muhammad Faraj Ahmed Bashmilah y Salah Nasser Salim ‘Ali, que estuvieron detenidos en secreto. Si la política estadounidense consiste en ceder toda la custodia y el control sobre los detenidos transferidos al control de otro gobierno, Estados Unidos debe manifestar claramente que éste es el caso respecto a estos tres hombres, y debe subrayar que Estados Unidos no ha puesto ninguna condición a su traslado;
- manifestar claramente que no se han puesto condiciones al traslado de Walid Muhammad Shahir Muhammad al-Qadasi, liberado de Guantánamo en abril de 2004 y que permanece detenido en Yemen sin cargos ni juicio;
- retirar todas las peticiones o exigencias al gobierno yemení para que mantenga detenidas a personas, a menos que sea con vistas a procesarlas sin demora por delitos comunes internacionalmente reconocibles y de acuerdo con las normas internacionales de justicia procesal;
- liberar a todas las personas que se encuentran detenidas bajo custodia estadounidense en lugares no desvelados, a menos que se las acuse de  delitos comunes internacionalmente reconocibles y se las procese sin demora y con las debidas garantías, de plena conformidad con las normas internacionales pertinentes, y sin recurrir a la pena de muerte;
- reafirme la prohibición absoluta de la tortura y otros tratos o penas crueles, inhumanos o degradantes, y deje claro a todos los agentes que participen en el trato o interrogatorio de detenidos y presos que esos actos están totalmente prohibidos y que toda persona implicada en ellos será procesada;
- investigue todas las denuncias de tortura y malos tratos de Muhammad Abdullah Salah al-Assad, Muhammad Faraj Ahmed Bashmilah y Salah Nasser Salim ‘Ali, y garantice que toda persona a la que se halle responsable de esos actos comparece ante la justicia;
- prohíba la devolución o el traslado de personas a lugares donde corran peligro de sufrir torturas u otros malos tratos;
- proporcionar plena reparación, que incluya restitución, indemnización, rehabilitación y satisfacción.

Estados Unidos debe poner fin a la práctica de la detención secreta. No es sólo que esas condiciones alienten la tortura y los malos tratos, sino que además el estar “desaparecido” de la faz de la Tierra sin saber por qué o durante cuánto tiempo constituye un delito en virtud del derecho internacional y es una experiencia que ninguna familia y ninguna persona debería vivir.
Gracias por su atención.

So when you take away one character in the scene of life, you have everything and everyone else remaining, but with a void. Everyone surrounding feel the effects. It is sad that I have almost memorized the recording on Krome Processing Center's menu about how they intend to adhere to us, the public in a "prompt, courteous, and professional manner". I've never laughed so hard in disbelief, for it was even a miracle to have someone answer the phone at Krome. But that's sad, very sad.

My point it is completely unnecessary for me to have been treated the way I have been for the last few weeks. There is no excuse what so ever. I was taught at the age of seventeen even at a part time job in the mall that you always have to come up with a solution. We were always taught that there was an alternate solution so one would say to the customer, "such and such might not work, BUT THIS IS WHAT I CAN DO FOR YOU…" I was taught that was your job as a professional. If part time employees at a mall can get this down then why can't federal government officials? Take pride in your work and do it well. Being who you are you take on a major role in how our country runs, and as a citizen I am very disappointed the way you serve as a  representation of America. 
Something needs to be done to fix this problem. I have never been a selfish person, never ask for much in life, but this struck a nerve and I would hope after reading this letter something be done. I am not happy, not happy at all, that this place I call my home, my beloved country would employ government officials who would ever treat anyone like they have.

Before deciding to separate, I checked with my base’s finance office at Scott Air Force Base to make sure I would be cleared to separate under the sole survivor act and not have to repay my bonus money. I was told by the person I spoke to that I would not have to repay the bonus money I received.  As I began to out-process the military I learned that I would have to pay back the military $4200 for the bonus money paid to me. 
 
I find it very unfair that I have to repay this money since people who have separated under the force reshaping program in addition to the ones who are being asked to voluntarily separate because of performance and behavioral issues do not have to repay bonus money paid to them without fulfilling their military obligations. 
 
When I found out I had to repay this money I immediately used my chain of command to request a waiver of repayment of the bonus money I received. Since this is an uncommon issue my commander did not know where to send my request after signing it so they forwarded it to the base legal office. After separating from the military I received a letter from Capt. Brock C. Cima from the Scott Air Force base legal office denying my request. Capt. Cima claims my commander did not have the authority to approve my request. HOWEVER, Capt. Cima DID NOT have the authority to DENY my request. After my former commander signed my request it was suppose to go to the Secretary of Defense to be granted a waiver.
 
I believe Capt. Cima acted incompetently by not sending my request to the appropriate official and by not taking in consideration the vast numbers of Air Force personnel who are separating from the military without repaying bonus money and completing their required military enlistment. 
 
It is a real insult to me and my family to loose my only sibling in the war then afterwards when I ask to separate because of my deployment status along with mental anguish to be forced to repay bonus money that I am not able to afford that others do not have to repay under the force reshaping act. If Capt. Cima had lost his only sibling while he himself was deployed maybe he would have looked further in the Air Force’s policy and realized that a waiver can be granted under my circumstances with approval. It was especially insulting that Capt. Cima insinuated in his recommendation letter that I reenlisted after hearing about my brother’s death to get the enlistment bonus when in reality my brother died two months after I reenlisted. If I could have foreseen my brother’s death I would have NEVER reenlisted.
 
My brother and I PROUDLY served our country and now the military has turned their back on us. I will be doing everything necessary to prove the military’s disregard to my family’s service and commitment including contacting the media if necessary. I will greatly appreciate any assistance you will provide.
 
Sincerely,
 
Mr. Timothy M. Gleason Jr. 
(Civilian)

From:	Richard Klein, MD, MPH <rdkleinmd@yahoo.com>
Sent:	Friday, November 24, 2006 11:38 AM
To:	Governor Jeb Bush
Subject:	Flawed Sustainable Growth Rate Formula

Richard Klein, MD, MPH
2605 W Tyson Ave
Tampa, FL 33611-4530


November 24, 2006

The Honorable Jeb Bush
Governor of Florida
The Capitol, 400 S. Monroe St.
Tallahassee, FL 32399-0001


Dear Governor Bush:

As a practicing plastic surgeon in your district, I am very concerned 
about the deep Medicare physician payment cuts expected in January.  I am 
writing to strongly urge you to stop these cuts and provide positive 
updates before the end of the year as well as seek a long-term solution to 
fix the Sustainable Growth Rate (SGR) formula.  Unless Congress acts, 
Medicare physician payment is expected to be cut about 5% a year, 
effective January 1, 2007, through 2015, totaling 37 percent!  When 
combined with the impact of other Medicare changes, many physicians such 
as me are facing combined cuts of 6 to 20 percent in 2007.

It is critical for patients and the physicians who serve them that you:

1) provide a positive update in 2007 to reflect increases in physician 
practice costs, per Medicare Payment Advisory Commission (MedPAC) 
recommendation to Congress, and

2) stop these drastic cuts and replace with a long-term formula that 
accurately reflects physicians' practice costs.

The continued stability of the Medicare program is at stake.  Additional 
cuts will result in a decline in Medicare and TRICARE patient access to 
care, reduction in the number of physicians willing to accept new Medicare 
patients, and states that lose millions in health care dollars.  As other 
plans tie their payment rates to Medicare rates, the impact will have 
far-reaching consequences for patients' access to care and place 
additional strains on physician practices who are already facing declining 
reimbursement, increased practice costs, and rising medical liability 
rates.

Time is running out.  Please act now.  Over 265 members of the U.S. House 
of Representatives and over 80 members of the United States Senate have 
signed letters this year urging that physicians be provided with a 
positive payment update in 2007.  

Stopping the SGR cut will assure that Medicare patients can continue to 
receive the care they depend on and deserve. 

Sincerely,


Richard D Klein, MD, MPH
813-326-4316

From: Governor Jeb Bush [mailto:Jeb.Bush@MyFlorida.com] 
Sent: Monday, November 20, 2006 4:49 PM
To: Vicki Kile-Wilson
Subject: RE: daylight savings

 

Florida Governor Jeb Bush thanks you for your e-mail about daylight saving time.  Governor Bush appreciates your expressing your opinion.

 

Many years ago, the Florida Legislature voted to comply with daylight saving time.  If you believe this decision should be changed, please contact the members of your local legislative delegation.  Any changes to the federal law itself, such as the date on which daylight saving time begins, would require an act of the U.S. Congress.

 

Since its inception, daylight saving time has been a topic for debate.  Many people have strong reasons to support or oppose daylight saving time.  For example, farmers and business people may favor it.  Parents, however, may express concern for the safety of their children going to or from school in darkness.  Those who feel strongly about daylight saving time as it applies to school attendance hours should contact members of the local school board.

 

Once again, thank you for sharing your concerns with Governor Bush.

 

Sincerely,

LD McDonald

Citizens’ Services

Office of the Governor

Thank you for your recent letter asking for assistance in obtaining 
affordable housing.
I appreciate the opportunity to respond.

As you may know, subsidized housing programs are under local and/or federal 
government control, and your best source of assistance is the executive 
director of the housing authority.  I suggest you write or call that person. 
  His or her address and telephone number can be found in the local 
government section of your telephone book.

I cannot help you with medicaire, that is a federal issue.  I am, however, I 
am forwarding your concerns to the Department of Children and families.  You 
may be eligible for medicaid, which is a state program.

The Florida Housing Finance Corporation's First Time Homebuyer Program makes 
purchasing a home more affordable for low-to-moderate income families and 
individuals by offering fixed, low-interest rate mortgage loans.  In 
addition, Florida Housing also offers up to $14,999 ($25,000 in high cost 
Counties) to assist eligible borrowers with their down payment and closing 
costs.  You can also obtain information on this program online at 
http://www.floridahousing.org/fthb/FirstTimeHomebuyers.aspx or by calling 
them at (850) 488-4197.

I hope this information is helpful, and if I can assist you with any other 
issue or concern, please let me know.

						Sincerely,



						Rex T. Newman
						Office of Citizens' Services

        My full name is Matthew J Dyas, (Alien # 077-921-993 just in case you need it) I'm originally from Drogheda,Co-Louth,Ireland. I left my home and all I had there and came to the U.S. on June 6th 2000 due to threats made on my families lives and my own. These threats were to burn my mothers house down with them in it(of course)!!!, if I did'nt get out.So i decided to flee to the U.S. I was admitted through J.F.K airport on a 90 day vacation visa. I am  very much aware that I broke the law by outstaying my time. When I moved to florida the INS caught up with me and detained me. This is when I told them about my situation back home, I was then interviewed by a  senior Immigration official who heard my case and released me on the basis that he believed I had a credible fear of being returned to my country.
     I then retained attorney  Mark Labate who turned out to be a disaster, not only did he fail to get my asylum application in on time, but he also classified me as an arriving alien which caused a lot of problems later on.
   Next I retained attorney Julio A Padilla a referral from another attorney called Frederick A Polatzek.. We went on to file a lozato motion to allow us to file a late application. This was granted by Judge Seymour Kleinfeld (who has since retired but not before denying my application). My Asylum case was based on the facts that I was conned into fundraising for a number of "charitable organizations" one of them was called HEADWAY which is an organization to help people and their families who suffered  losses from head injuries. 
     This particular one was close to my heart as my younger brother Robert had not long passed due to a brain tumor. We also were fund raising for the Irish deaf society and others like the Irish arts and crafts foundation. Four or five vehicles would leave the agency based in  Drogheda every day and cross the border into Northern Ireland. Sometimes, certain individuals would be dropped off before crossing the border. This I found to be strange. On a number of occasions we were stopped by British patrols and questioned, shortly after I realized that the drivers were using radio to avoid  police checkpoints. Then came the day when I was arrested and interrogated by the R.U.C.(formerly The Royal Ulster Constabulary) When the R.U.C. were satisfied that I had no idea what I was involved in, they informed me that these people were in fact using this as a cover up to fund an illegal organization and I was in serious danger of being falsely imprisoned. I was furious. The following day I went to the head of the agency and told him what had happened to me and that I was going to contact the Irish Independant Newspaper to try and expose the whole operation.
 This was all happening in 1998 before the good friday aggreement. From that day on , the threats began.They went from an isolated verbal incident to a number of brutal attacks on me. All of which were reported to the police by my family and I. Then came the threats toward my family which scared the hell out of me. I never did expose them for fear of my life but i did name a few names at my Immigration Master Hearing. "One of those people I named at my hearing has just recently been caught with hundreds of thousands of dollars worth of drugs, the same amount in cash and a small arsenal of automatic weapons, October 2006 (Paul Reay) ".MY CASE WAS DENIED. We then filed an appeal and soon after I got married to an american citizen.  About a year or so  later MY APPEAL WAS DENIED. Since we had already filed for an i130, we then filed for a greencard on the basis of marriage. That,s when my first attorney's screw up came into play and because he classified me as an arriving alien and I was considered not eligible to adjust my status. Finally we got all that taken care of and everything was looking great and it was just a matter of time untill I got my greencard.
  I have been married over two and a half years now and the i130 has not even been approved yet! and guess what , my marriage seems to be coming to an end soon.
                                                        So, to try and sum it all up: I have been here six and a half years. 'Right now'!!! I'm married to an American citizen. For all this time I have had a valid drivers license,(never got a ticket), valid work authorization, valid social security#, health and dental insurance for myself and my wife.I have never claimed a cent from any governmental agency or charity!!!!.  I schooled myself  for certifications with the American Indoor Air Quality Council, I hold the professional titles of a Council Certified Indoor Environmentalist, a Council  Certified Microbial Remediator, I am also certified with the IICRC in Fire and Smoke Restoration.I manage a restoration department with a nationwide franchise called Coit services. I have been a law abiding, tax paying member of church and community and I believe I provide a vital service to the residents of south Florida. I have also obtained my high school diploma (again), just so I could go to college here, to learn spanish. This year I became a published poet. my work was published in a hard back book called Twilight Musings. It was dedicated to september 11th and I sent a copy to the First Lady and President as a gift (I really hope they get to see it someday). I was published again just recently by Noble House Publishing Inc.located in the Empire State Building. Recently I've been in contact with Navy and Army recruiters as I am willing to serve and die for this country MY HOME that I love. All I would like in return is a chance to earn the privilege to become a legal resident and eventually a proud American citizen. 
       I thought with all my heart I would win my asylum case. After the master hearing the prosecuting attorney said outside "it's nothing to do with your predicament, it' all about politics!!!!!!!!  They said if the judge had granted asylum they would not have opposed his decision. 
                                      Govenor, I am running out of  faith, money$$$$!!!!!!and nerves I have spent thousands( at least $35,000) on this procedure over the years and to be honest sometimes I feel like I'm on the verge of a nervous breakdown..Sorry to sound so dramatic but it's been a long hard struggle and the words of swift justice play in my mind a lot. I 'm trying my very best to make things right for 6 years now. I am five and a half years sober and proud of it, but I was hoping life would be a little easier for me now, although I do know it could be a lot worse! and I am a thankful person.
           I have tried to seek help in a number of ways. The Irish Lobby for Immigration Reform informed me that they can only help the "undocumented" and not someone like myself  who is trying to do everthing the proper way!!!! this to me seems unbelievable.

21 August 2006  - Immediate Release

 

H.R. 3072 - A Bill to Revive the System of Parole for Federal Prisoners 

 

Subject:  American Correctional Association  (ACA) Resolution on the Reinstatement of a System of Parole for Federal Prisoners. 

A resolution supporting federal legislation for the "Reinstatement of a System of Parole for Federal Prisoners" was unanimously passed by the American Correctional Association Delegate Assembly on Wednesday, 16 August 2006, in Charlotte, North Carolina.  

 

 

To wit:

 

WHEREAS, a substantial number of Federal inmates are nonviolent drug offenders with long sentences and the majority of this segment of the inmate population is being incarcerated for the first time; and

 

WHEREAS, some Federal inmates are serving life sentences without the possibility of parole for nonviolent offenses; and

 

WHEREAS, parole has been eliminated in the Federal system; and

 

WHEREAS, offenders can be rehabilitated and should be given a second chance to lead productive lives; and

 

WHEREAS, prison crowding is a danger to both inmates and staff; and

 

WHEREAS, the cost to house inmates increases substantially with age; and

 

WHEREAS, a Federal agency with inmate release jurisdiction exists to protect public safety;

THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the American Correctional Association urges Congress to reinstate and fully fund a system of parole for Federal prisoners.

 

American Correctional Association

From:	Manyvone Champavannarath <crazymany94@verizon.net>
Sent:	Wednesday, November 8, 2006 1:13 PM
To:	Governor Jeb Bush
Subject:	Stop the nightmare of 11/15/2006
Attachments:	Manyvonecrop.JPG

I am writing to strongly communicate the need to delay the new Medicare Power Mobility Fee Schedule published by the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) scheduled for an November 15, 2006 implementation.  

As published, these drastic price reductions will limit and deny access to medically appropriate power mobility products and services for Medicare beneficiaries, especially those beneficiaries with severe disabilities.  This will not only hurt Medicare beneficiaries, but also children and other adults with complex disabilities that require this equipment to meet their daily medical and functional needs.

For almost three years now CMS, physicians, clinicians, consumers, providers, and manufacturers have worked on improvements and safeguards to the Medicare power mobility benefit.  However, given the drastic cuts in the reimbursement amounts it appears that all this time and effort may be undermined by a rush to implement changes before key issues are resolved and an appropriate implementation period is provided.  Moving forward without making the required corrections and allowing an appropriate time period for implementation will create major access problems for Medicare beneficiaries and others.  

The new fee schedule drastically reduces reimbursement for complex rehab products used by severely disabled consumers by up to 33% or more.  These products are used by beneficiaries with severe diagnoses such as ALS, muscular dystrophy, cerebral palsy, spinal cord injury and severe brain injury.  These reductions will eliminate the availability of the appropriate power wheelchair and service required by Medicare beneficiaries and other individuals with complex disabilities. 

In developing the new fee schedule, CMS utilized a pricing methodology that has been universally recognized as flawed.  In fact, CMS itself has admitted the methodology does not work and is in the process of putting a new methodology in place.  As an example of the problems, the fee schedule provides that a Group 2 power wheelchair (less complex) will be reimbursed at a higher rate than a Group 3 power wheelchair (more complex).  

These changes are the most dramatic since the establishment of the power mobility benefit under Medicare: 64 new codes, new pricing, new coverage criteria, and new documentation requirements.  How can these possibly be implemented effectively and smoothly with such a short period of time for physician and clinician education and the major operational and educational changes required within each Medicare provider’s operation?

Given the significant concerns being expressed by all stakeholders- physicians, clinicians, consumers, providers, and manufacturers- I respectfully but strongly request that the November 15, 2006 effective date for the published pricing and coverage policies be postponed until all identified issues are resolved.  Once these issues are resolved, the revised information can then be published and a 120 day implementation period provided to allow for a smooth transition.

To rush ahead without fixing the issues and problems that have been identified will undermine all the time and effort of the past three years and hurt the ability of Medicare beneficiaries and others with disabilities to access medically appropriate mobility equipment.

My name is Manyvone Champavannarath, but everyone calls me Many or Speedy.  Different people have different names for me. Most people call me a giggle box because I love to laugh. I was born 32 years ago with severe cerebral palsy (CP). I grew up in Central Florida, where my family settled after leaving Laos.
 
I graduated from high school with high honors in 1994. I loved high school. After high school I went straight to college where I graduated with my Associate’s Degree in Business Administration in 1999.  
 
In 1997, I moved into my own apartment with a roommate to help with the bills.  I have caretakers who come in and out to do things for me. I moved out because I wanted to be independent and I wanted to do things like go hang out with my friends. I wanted to be like a normal 23 year old girl. This was one of the best things I have done.
 
In 1998, I became involved with the church near my house.  I am doing more with my church now.  During the week I run errands around the church. I working with youth group every Sunday night.  I help teach Sunday School Class every Sunday morning. I help out with middle schoolers one Friday a month.  
 
I tutor a second grader at an after school program once a week at church. I am on the Administrative Board at church that meets every quarter. I am on the Youth Council that meet once a month. I am on the Welcome Committee at church. I go visit people at the nursing home for the church when I have time. 

I don’t think lawmakers realized how much the disable have to depend on power wheelchairs.   This is due to the fact that they have no clue what it’s like to be in a wheelchair for 16 hours a day for the rest of their life.  

My wheelchair is the most essential part of my life.  It gives me independence and the best quality of life.  If the new guidelines go through, I will be a prisoner in my own home!! This new guidelines will take my legs away!!!!

I’m begging you not to make us disabled suffer anymore than we already are!!!!

Crying out for help to stop this nightmare,
Manyvone

November 6, 2006 

Honorable Governor Bush: 

I am writing this letter on behalf of my husband, Ovil Osmark Hernandez Cruz to respectfully ask for your help.  I am a citizen of the United States and was born in 1970 in Rockville Center, NY.  

Ovil has been detained without cause by INS in the Krome Immigration Services Detention Center in Miami after appearing for a hearing on Thursday, November 3, 2006 after many years of fighting to stay in this country.  He is not a flight risk and has shown up for every hearing that he has been scheduled to appear at.  We are a family of 4 at the moment, but are expecting our 3rd child which is due in the next few weeks.  I cannot make it through the end of this pregnancy or the rest of my life without Ovil with me.  If INS is allowed to keep him I don’t know how I will make it through the delivery of our expected child.  If they are allowed to deport him we will loose everything we have fought so hard to build for our family, our home and his job.  The stress we are all under during this period is of course very high.  My children seem to be suffering the worst from this.  Our 8 year old is a little easier to explain this to, but our 2 year old really doesn’t understand and only cries for her Papa when she doesn’t find him during the day.

He is currently employed with Volvo Aero Services here in Boca Raton, FL and has held this job steadily for at least the last 9 years.  He has been awarded promotions within the company and even was given the award of Employee of the Month in October of 2004.

Ovil’s situation is one that is very disheartening.  He not only has a blemish on his record, but is also fighting INS not to deport him back to Guatemala.  Ovil is not yet a citizen of the United States, but a Permanent Resident seeking United States Citizenship.  His Mother, Father and Sister have all become United States Citizens, yet he is still fighting for this freedom.  They came to the United States in the early 1980’s because of the violence in their former country of Guatemala.

We have submitted a request for Pardon on August 11, 2006 to the Office of Executive Clemency regarding Ovil's case which we hope will get reviewed and approved with the circumstances surrounding the case.

Over ten years ago Ovil was charged with lewd assault on a minor.  The circumstances surrounding the case were quite simple.  Ovil met a girl and one thing lead to another and they spent the night together.  The girl ended up to be less than 18 years old and her parents pushed to press charges against Ovil in denial that their daughter was having consensual sexual relations at a young age.  Once the parents realized that their daughter was not telling the truth regarding the story they decided to drop the charges, but it was too late.  The State decided to press the charges because of the type of case it was.  He pled no contest to the charges.  Ovil was sentenced to 5 years probation, which he served and was released without any trouble.  During those 5 years though he was arrested and taken to Manatee County because INS wants to deport him.  He now lives the life of a Sexual Offender in the shadows of people that might think the worst of him if they were to find out without knowing the circumstances surrounding the case.

We understand the severity of the conviction against Ovil, but don’t understand how a country that protects its people could allow something so horrible to leave a black mark on the life of one young person who made one very big mistake.  Should a person that has made one mistake pay with his entire life?  Ovil is not a Sexual Offender in the true sense of the description.  Yet he must follow the guidelines set for people who knowingly cause harm to others when he poses no threat to society.  He must register twice a year so that the State of Florida knows where he lives at all times.  Police Officers show up at home to make sure he’s still living there.  He cannot go on field trips with his daughters because school volunteers must pass a background check.  Even though there has never been, either before the conviction or after, any other accusation, the label of Sexual Offender follows Ovil with all of its harshness. 

For the first 2 ½ years of our marriage Ovil suffered from Anxiety and Panic Attacks which he received medical treatment for.  He has since gotten himself off all of the medication he was taking, but still suffers with Anxiety on a daily basis.  The Panic Attacks have subsided, thank God, but there are no guarantees that they will never return.  The attacks were brought on by the stress related to all of this hanging over Ovil’s head.  He thinks everyday what life will be like if INS deports him.  He thinks about where he’ll live, if he’ll even make it, if he’ll be able to get a job, if he’ll ever see his family again and if he’ll ever be able to hold us in his arms feeling the security that a wife and children can bring to your life.  It is not only scary for him, but for all of us too.  Ovil is the backbone of our household.  I do not know how we will survive if he is not here with us.  He helps his parents and sister, niece and nephew not only by being there for them in times of need, but monetarily as well.

I will not write this letter and tell you that Ovil has never done anything in his life wrong, but I will tell you that in the 7 years that I know him he has done nothing unlawful.  He has the utmost respect for me and our children.  One of which is my daughter from a previous marriage and the other is our daughter together.  Our family will not be complete if Ovil is deported.  Our children will loose their father and I will loose my husband & best friend.  He is a hard working, faithful and honest person, the kind of person America would be proud to call a Citizen.

Please Governor Bush, review this matter and help my husband in any way you can. 

Thank you for taking the time to read this letter.

Sincerely, 
Vita Hernandez

From:	Manyvone Champavannarath <crazymany94@verizon.net>
Sent:	Saturday, November 4, 2006 9:38 PM
To:	Governor Jeb Bush
Subject:	Urgent matter
Attachments:	New chair.JPG

Dear Governor Bush,

I urge you to take immediate action to stop the devastating changes to the Medicare Power Mobility Device (PMD) benefit scheduled to take effect on November 15. The planned changes will severely restrict access to the power wheelchairs many people with disabilities need to live independent lives and participate fully in society.

In August, the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) issued a final local coverage determination (LCD) for power mobility devices which places strict limits on access to “Group 3” power wheelchairs, the type of wheelchairs often needed by those with long term disabilities and chronic conditions.

CMS has also issued new reimbursement levels for these Group 3 wheelchairs which will cut reimbursements by up to 40 percent. These cuts will likely translate into serious access problems for beneficiaries as many providers say they will be unable to provide these high-end devices to Medicare beneficiaries at the new reimbursement levels.

Both of these changes are scheduled to take effect on November 15, 2006.  Access to appropriate mobility devices is essential to allowing persons with mobility impairments to live independently, to work, and to participate in community life. I am always out in the community doing things. My wheelchair gives me independence and the BEST quality of life.  Without my wheelchair I would be a prisoner in my own home!!!!!!

Thanks,
Manyvone Champavannarath

I called to register him for Medicare, (after all, he is on disability, right???) only to find out he is not eligible for 2 years AFTER he began receiving his SSI payments, (which is 2 1/2 years from his approval date!)  I am floored! Clearly, this makes no sense.  If someone is on disability, obviously, he can't work and there are significant pre-existing conditions. If there are pre-existing conditions, no one wants to insure you, and if they do, the coverage is limited and the premiums are "through the roof", especially considering he is on a fixed income.  I made calls to several private health insurance carriers and even IF they are willing to cover him, the premiums are unaffordable.
 
The Social Security Office suggested applying for Medicaid, but already told me that his income is to high for assistance.  That also is ironic because if he has to pay what I have been quoted for health insurance, then his income qualifies him as poverty level.
 
I guess my question to you is: How can someone on disability not qualify for Medicare and what can be done to get him insured right away?  I have left 2 messages at the Medicaid office, but have not yet received a call back.  I currently live in Central Florida, but have plans to go to South Florida this weekend to help Phil sort this out. I took the day off work Friday so we can go to the Medicaid office , if necessary, but since I haven't heard back from them, I am not sure if this is a wasted trip.
 
If you need more information from me as to Phil's condition, or specific research I have done, I will be happy to provide that to you.  All I know is he cannot be without health insurance and if Medicare or Medicaid are not available to him because of flaws in state & federal laws, he and others like him should not be the ones to suffer and we need to know what to do.
 
Please help.
 
By the way, I mean this sincerely...it has been a pleasure and honor having you as this State's Governor.  A greatly admire you and your entire family and look forward to seeing you in the White House in the near future.
