Dear Sir,
 
We began the Naturalization Application Process for my husband in September, 2004. The process took little or no time from the applications beginning until the request was made and given for the final interview and fingerprint taking.  This process took 7 month, with fingerprints taken in April 2005.  He was told at that time, that the process turnaround for finalization and confirmation of Naturalization was about 60 to 90 days, but it could be longer depending on backlogs. Several times during our wait, we called to inquire about his case, my husband was told, and “it was still pending.”  
 
15 months later, he finally spoke with a representative over the phone who explained that his “fingerprints had expired.”  In June, 2006, we drove back to Jacksonville so that he could have his fingerprints redone.  At the time of our trip, the Immigration clerk informed him that it was an error on the part of Homeland Security / Naturalization that his file “sat on a shelf and was never submitted.”  She explained that “it should only be a matter of 30 to 60 days and that he should hear something soon since it has been almost 2 years.”  My husband has inquired twice since his last visit and the last letter we received is enclosed.
 
My husband has been a permanent legal resident alien since 1984.  He has worked in this country for 20 years; he has paid taxes, paid into Social Security, Medicare and Medicaid.  He is currently a student studying Graphic Design at Santa Fe Community College in Gainesville and has student loans. All of his family that arrived here with him from Peru has applied and passed through the Naturalization Process in a matter of months, they are all US Citizens.  
 
I am writing to you as a Citizen, as a tax payer as registered voter, as his wife. I am frustrated with this process.  It has been ongoing for 25 months and now we might have to pay another $300.00 to have his permanent alien card renewed.  We are both students and working people.  We do not make a lot of money. I understand, especially since 9/11, that the process has become more stringent and things are looked at more closely, however we have done everything legally requested by the laws of the state of Florida and the United States concerning the Naturalization process to no resolve.
 
I am writing to you and asking your help with his case.  We do not know where to turn at his point and we are worried that we are receiving the same treatment as before and his file is sitting on a shelf again. 
We understand that this is a busy time of year and our request seems minimal to others, but, it is an important to us.  If you can help us we would greatly appreciate it.
 
Thank you for your time and we hope to hear from you soon.
 
Sincerely Yours,
 
 
 
Jorge H. Eran

Sir,								26 October 2006



I am writing in regards to the proposed move of the 46th Test Wing to
Edwards AFB.  Repeatedly, AFMC leadership has ignored the facts surrounding
the cost effectiveness of this initiative.  Their personal agendas are quite
clear.  When the initial story leaked in the newspapers first there was
denial, then partial truths and then the story of their “experts” had
reviewed this move and verified its cost effectiveness.  To now allow this
same group of people to conduct yet another analysis to determine if the
move to California is cost effective is truly a case of putting the fox in
charge of the hen house.  A transition team remains in place at Eglin and
taskings are being worked daily to try and validate the original assumptions
made by AFMC leadership regarding the move.  Additionally,
the cost analysis needs to address the costs associated with moving and the
subsequent costs associated with the 53rd Wing.  As this is not AFMC, it
will be book kept elsewhere, but it is still a cost to the US Air Force.
The bottom line is that is will cost well over 100 million dollars to build
the infrastructure at Edwards to “bed down” Eglin aircraft and equipment.
This does not even address the costs required to support a stand alone 53rd
Wing.  One of the truly ironic parts of this initiative is that it seriously
reduces or eliminates many aspects of our national Weapons Test and
Evaluation capability…and it seems that AFMC leadership is OK with that.
The military leadership in Air Force Material Command is moving ahead full
steam with this ill thought out plan and I hope and pray that you remain
vigilant to their actions.  Unless someone directly tells the AFMC
leadership to “knock it off” I fear they will continue to do all in their
power to bring this move to fruition.  It may be time to ask your brother to
intervene and stop this dangerous and faulty plan.

Thank you for your continued support.



David L. de Vos

Dear Governor Bush:
As a political sympathizer and admirer of your efforts
and actions in the state of Florida, I would like to
respectfully ask for you advice, guidance and if
possible assistance on a very delicate situation.
It concerns my immediate family’s wellbeing and legal
immigration status in Florida and the United States. 
The following is the background to better illustrate
the situation and justify the origin of my request.
I’m a US Legal Permanent Resident since 1987, with a
University of Central Florida Business degree and over
12 years of professional experience in the
telecommunications industry. I have held an executive
position with Comcast Cable Communications of West
Florida for the past three years, and having worked
overseas during the last decade I got married and have
a wife and three children all born in Guatemala City.
In April 2003 I choose provide my family with more and
better opportunities by relocating them to Florida as
a result of unemployment and the political and
economical turmoil that prevailed in Latin America. At
that time and based on my Legal Permanent Resident
status I was advised by the US Embassy in Guatemala
City to travel to the US with non-immigrant visas for
my family and proceed to petition for legal residency
when in country. Following those instructions, in
October 2003 I filed the required petitions and
received the approved petition notices in October
2005. Since receiving the approval notices the process
has almost come to a halt, I have not been able to
secure any information or updates on what to do or who
to contact in order to expedite and complete the
process. With all the immigration controversy lately
in the news we fear our petitions may get lost and our
status indefinitely unresolved.
My family and I lead a very busy and involved life in
this great state of Florida. My wife is an orthodontic
surgeon unable to legally work and financially
contribute to our household, so she takes care of the
children and volunteers both at the elementary school
and the local library system. My children despite
being young participate in many extracurricular
activities at school and in the community. My oldest
son at 9 years, has been since enrolling in school an
A student and involved in Student Council; just
recently receiving the principals award for
outstanding citizenship.
I would like nothing more than to be able to securely
provide for my family and for them to enjoy of all the
rights, privileges and obligations that being a legal
US Citizen entitles them to.
Can you please refer me to someone within your office
that can help move on with the process so my children
can soon become legal and productive citizens of this
great country?

With all my respect and gratitude,

Maurice Amaya

Classic case of federal interference--the flood insurance program was a boondoggle from the start and now because some people naturally took advantage of it by re-building in true flood areas, the rest of us are being penalized when we did not build in a risk area and when we chose obviously high ground to build upon. Why are those of us living inland, high and dry having to pay for other’s idiocy !? 

I have been a Republican  for years,  but I have not seen an improvement at all in government spending or costs such as this. Anything the federal government touches turns to a sorry, expensive mess and as I see it, the Republican Congress can only be improved by getting some ‘real’ businesspeople and homeowners, etc. to represent us and scale back this travesty in Washington, which IS a true swampland.

I suspect Congress mandates it because too many claims were made upon Congress’ own flood insurance entitlement experiment. A citizen should not be required to spend hundreds to show FEMA its map is inaccurate and we should not have to buy FEMA’s new flood maps because they choose not to put them online–their own people could not even send me the proper map for my home when I gave them the ‘old’ map number as a guide! Craig:

working visa.  It has become very difficult to change our status to 
residents, and therefore Penpower/GE will not be able to help me with 
this.  As a matter of fact we called several lawyers and no one is willing 
to represent us.  Because we both have college degrees, speak fluent 
English and I have a good job, we are labeled as “displacing an American 
out of a good job” and therefore not allowed to stay beyond our temporary 
worker status. 

As a last resource we are trying to get the Oprah Winfrey production team 
involved to research the way the immigration cases are handled and see if 
we can find a solution to our problem.

Social unrest in Argentina is on the rise. Our return to Argentina, even 
if temporary, represents a high risk of kidnapping for our child because 
of her accent she could easily be mistaken for an American.  We are trying 
to avoid running this risk and therefore would like to stay in America and 
continue to enjoy our freedom and pursue of happiness.  The American 
people have been amazing hosts and most people do not want us to go.

We have applied for Canadian residency, but this process may take many 
months, even several years and we would rather stay in America than having 
to start all over again.  

Here is a link to Oprah.  Scroll down on this web page and, please send 
her a note letting her know that you would like us to be able to stay in 
the country.  It is very important that you start the message with 
“Regarding Silvina Lanusse and Carlos Helou from Argentina”.

Message to Oprah:

Regarding Silvina Lanusse and Carlos Hélou

Dear Oprah:

Two days ago my wife, Silvina Lanusse wrote to you regarding our status in 
the US.  We are a couple from Argentina with a 10-year-old daughter.  We 
both dreamt of immigrating to the US for as long as we can remember.  We 
both learned and speak English fluently and we both hold college degrees 
from good American colleges.  We were student in Massachusetts in the late 
80’s and early 90’s.  After college and when our student visa came to an 
end we returned to Argentina, were we both gathered valuable work 
experience and in 2001, a few days before 9/11, I was invited to work in 
the US.  Since then I have been involved in Wind Energy with GE, and I 
feel honored to have help America become more “green.”  Our child is an 
amazing student and my wife, because she does not have a working permit, 
has been volunteering her time in schools and other activities in order to 
give more than what we take.  America has been a great host and we are 
very happy living here in freedom and in the pursue of happiness.  By now 
our daughter is as American as apple pie.

Next March (2007) our second consecutive working visa will expire and we 
will have to leave the country.  Immigration processes have become so 
cumbersome, that even though the company I work for would like me to 
continue working with them, they have discourage me from trying to become 
a resident.  I can’t blame them, given the difficulty of this process.  I 
have called several other lawyers and no one is willing to offer their 
services. They believe we do not have a case.  We are being punished for 
having an education and being labeled as “displacing an American out of a 
good job”.  Curiously enough, my traveling job is not very attractive to 
the average worker, but it is difficult to prove that to the authorities.

The State of Florida has right now a shortage of teachers.  My wife has 
excellent teaching skills and a passion for children that could be very 
valuable.  However, the state is not willing to work towards her 
residency.  It simply makes no sense.  

While hundreds of thousands of illegal immigrant cross the borders every 
year, settle down in America and stay with all benefits, people like us 
are denied a two months extension for my child to finish school.  We 
refused to stay in an illegal status, for we believe that we must not 
disrespect our host country.  However our future looks grim. Social unrest 
is on the rise in Argentina and life down there has become very dangerous, 
particularly for a young girl with an American accent.  The possibilities 
for us down there are very limited to none.  On the other hand we believe 
we are the type of immigrants that America can benefit from, people with 
an open mind, no political or religious agenda and willingness to work 
hard and always try to give to our community more then we take. 

We are writing to you, not only in regards to our particular case, but in 
behalf of the many educated immigrants that are of great value to America 
and are not given the chance to stay because of their unwillingness to be 
illegal immigrant and break the law.  It is almost like reverse 
discrimination.  Educated people are given fewer chances then other 
immigrants.

Please, consider having a program were we can expose this situation and 
find a more humane solution to this problem, while helping America keep 
its skilled immigrant work force.    Thank you,

Carlos Helou



As a veteran of "Iraqi Freedom" in the US Navy I would like think that if 
someone tries to do it the correct way that they would be rewarded.  So 
Mr. Governor can you please help our frienda stay in our beloved Country.  

Sincerely,


Craig Mazurowski

Dear Governor Bush,

The motive behind this letter obtains concern for our father's immigration 
situation, or lack there of. Our father, Francisco Javier Lopez, arrived to 
the United States of America in the year of 1981. A Nicaraguense, born and 
raised, he arrived to the states due to political upheavals occurring in 
Nicaragua throughout the eighties. A father of four American born citizen 
daughters, whom are so rightfully writing this letter, are in mere disbelief 
of the process that our father is undergoing to receive his residency. Our 
father is a responsible man living in the United States, whom has paid his 
taxes and dues, and does not take this country’s opportunities for granted. 
My father is only guilty for his determination, and thrive to live the 
typical American dream, which only America fully depicts. Due to 
bureaucracy, my father has been limited in obtaining the privilege of 
becoming an American
citizen, or even successfully proceeding with the process of becoming one.

   Our father, Francisco, arrived to his final interview with the INS in May 
of this year. During this interview,the INS coordinator brought hope to our 
family, by assuring that our fathers’ matter will be taken care of. It was 
said he would be receiving his alien card within ten days, 240 hours to be 
exact. She even proceeded with recording our fathers’ finger prints. 
Unexpectedly, absolutely nothing came, absolutely nothing was received, and 
a sense of worry and concern began to fill the atmosphere of this ceaseless 
situation. Our parents decided to bring the obstacle to a higher standard. 
They contacted local congressman Mario Diaz Balart merely to receive 
disappointing news that our fathers file is presently placed in a desk 
filled with large amounts of other applicant’s applications, as it had been 
before the "progress" had been made. It was also said that it was up to the 
mercy of the INS to review his file. Apparently, the progress our father has 
made in the attempt to receive his residency came down to pieces upon 
greeting those unsatisfactory reports.

   Our father has found himself in a critical direction, and his four 
daughters are determined to raise any measure it takes to help him receive 
the residency that he has rightfully earned. Our father complied with 
absolutely every aspect of this process, and though we know that patience is 
a crucial factor in the citizenship process, please bear in mind that we are 
discussing over twenty years of my father residing in this country, and six 
of those twenty years of him sitting around in the same spot. On behalf of 
Francisco Javier Lopez, we do not want to see our father wait around 
anymore, and we do not appreciate INS coordinators pulling my father back 
and forth as if he was some kind of ignorant fool. Do understand that my 
fathers file has been placed in the INS office since the year 2000. Despite 
everything else written, there have been two very frustrating occurrences in 
which our fathers’ immigration situation has been caught in the way of our 
family resolving matters. An uncle of the family, who lives in Nicaragua, 
had found his health in a sudden and extremely critical condition. Our uncle 
was placed in extreme intensive care in a nearby hospital, this past April. 
As a family, we understood that it was more than appropriate to embark on an 
urgent trip to Nicaragua to sit right by a relative that was going through 
severe health obstacles. Unfortunately, the trip had been cut down to five, 
due to my fathers’ inability to participate in such an emergency trip, and 
was not present at a time where his presence served as vital importance. My 
father pleaded for a re-entry and had to pay one-hundred and sixty dollars. 
He was still not able to participate in such a significant trip back to 
Nicaragua. The second occurrence occurred during the middle of this summer. 
Our fathers’ license has been expired since July 2006. While in the process 
of renewing his license, the DMV informed our father that he needed original 
documents from the INS to support that he is fully entitled to reside in 
this country. In simple terms, my father was prohibited to receive his new 
license due to the very troublesome and changeless case with these 
immigration matters. Just for your awareness, our father lives a hectic 
maintained schedule, and driving is a necessity for his daily activities and 
responsibilities, such as going to work, running errands, dropping off his 
children, etc.

   With all that is expressed in this letter, you may understand why we have 
chosen to contact and write this letter to you. We anticipate to witness you 
lend out your hand and help our father as well as our family; the 
opportunity to behold our father live up to his goal to become an American 
citizen, along with attaining a peace of mind that he has so rightfully 
earned. We understand that there are plenty other applicants in the same 
position as my father, but this matter has passed boundaries, and has come 
to a point where my father is unable to drive, or even visit Nicaragua at 
times where his presence is valued and needed. Our father is a responsible, 
accountable, competent individual that has been limited, confined, and 
restricted to meet and accomplish all of his wondrous expectations. Not to 
mention, that he has been lied to and treated as a fool a number of times. 
So do not misconstrue the bluntness we have chosen to apply to this letter. 
If you can bear in mind that we are vivid, and adequate American citizens 
which have taken advantage of our freedom of expression to help enable and 
support our father to reach one of his most important and urgent objectives. 
As daughters of a man that has been restricted and confined, we will go to 
no limit, and proudly label ourselves as tough customers who will stop at 
nothing. The answer “no” or no actions made to resolve this situation will 
not be acknowledged. Our entire family has always supported and been loyal 
to the Republican Party, in which two of us have already declared our 
encouragement. I hope you gather this letter with much consideration and 
appreciation, and we are anticipated to be approached with positive answers, 
and a soon resolution to this matter. We are American citizens filled with 
apprehension, hope, and faith to hear from you soon, and to finally grant 
our father a goal that he is beyond adequate to deserve. We appreciate your 
time and expected consideration. Thank you.

Francisco Javier Lopez

According to this lady, the Spanish speaking people of the US are going to demand that all public facilities - like hospitals, courthouses, etc. - be staffed by people who read, speak and comprehend Spanish. 
 
Incase you are not aware of it, some public schools in the New York area have already been designated "bilingual" and have already laid off teachers with seniority in order to hire new Spanish speaking (licensed bilingual) teachers.  
If you and your children intend to survive in your country (USA) you will have to become fluent in Spanish or risk the consequences.
 
We hear about the silent majority but I think we are going to have to speak up or find ourselves a conquered country.  That would be an interesting historical note - greatest land in the world conquered by Mexico without ever firing a shot!  Think about it.

2. Petition to Require citizenship to be eligible for social services in the United States. 

3. No amnesty and No free services for illegal immigrants. 

4. Vote in English only, and Drivers test in English only.
Do we want to wind up like Canada where EVERYTHING has to be written in 2 languages?

DEEP IN THE HEART
 
                                                                     By: Driftin' AaronG
 
 
Deep in the heart of America stands a man
He's for all the people an' does more than any man can
 
He sacrifices all of himself to do what is right
And after the terrorist attack he took it to their homeland to fight
 
There are some that condemn an' say he's wrong
But true Americans stand with him singing a Freedom Song
 
Most of us know that President Bush is on the right track
Fighting for freedom an' liberty for all we can never turn back
 
So on with you Hugo Chavez and the U.N.
Rant an' Rave you cowardly foes for with you the devil has always been
 
In the end America an' her allies will win
An' the terrorists they'll cry out in pain as they fall to the depths of their sin
 
With this chosen land of liberty making the world all free
An' George Bush standin' tall an' proud seein' all nations a better place to be
 
Like his father before him there's no back up in George Bush's bones
He keeps his word even when liberals continue to cast their evil stones
 
And when this terrible war is over an' done now
America standin' proud with a bright new star upon her brow
 
So let some of the world and even some of our own put us down
In the end George W. Bush and heaven's glorious trumpet will sound
 
Like much of the past the bad people of the world have had their say
In the end it's always the same and America with divine liberty wins out the day

Dear Governor Bush,

 

I write as a concerned United Kingdom citizen who is a home owner in Kissimmee, Florida.

 

We have owned a short-term rental home in Florida for over 12 years and even in the awful aftermath of 9/11 found that we could rent our home easily. However, with the continuing problems with US Immigration this is becoming more and more difficult.

 

Many of our regular renters from the UK are refusing to come to the US as they feel that they are being treated so badly at Immigration. I may say that I do agree as the change in the attitude of many of the Immigration Officers is totally shocking. As one of my regulars said to me ‘we are being treated like shit now. 

 

Those of who are doing our best to keep the tourists coming to Florida are despairing. It will not be the end of the world for us if we have to sell our home, we bought when prices were low and even in these difficult times we would see a large profit. We can then take our money home and buy in Europe where we at least would be welcome. The point is that we do not want to do that. Many of us have spent a great deal of money in promoting tourism in Florida and we love Florida but if things continue as they are we will have no option but to sell up.

 

This should be a great time for tourism in Florida, with the British Pound strong against the US Dollar, the British should be keen to come to Florida and the rest of the US, but that is not the case. The latest suggestion that people would have to obtain a Visa, rather than use the Visa Waiver Programme is also a consideration. It would add a considerable amount to a holiday if a family had to pay the cost of Visas and also if they live outwith the London area there is also the cost of travelling there to obtain their Visas and probably overnight accommodation. This would definitely keep all but the most fervent tourist out of the US.

 

Immigration is not the only problem that we are facing; we are now being treated as second class in the Local Tax applications. This does not just affect those of us from the UK; it also affects short-term rental owners from parts of the US too. Osceola County has just approved a huge increase in taxes and of course those of us who are non-residents fare worse than local residents.

 

You must realise that it is the tourists that we short-term rental owners bring in that put the most into the economy, without the tourists the County would really have problems. Who spends the money in local stores and amusement parks? It is certainly not the locals. 

 

We are now also being penalised after all these years of having Florida Driving Licenses in that we have to re-apply each time we come rather than being allowed to renew as in the past.  I am well aware of all the security implications, but surely with a track record in the State and with all the modern technology available it should surely be possible for us to be security vetted and once you are satisfied with our clearance, be allowed to renew our licenses as in the past. This cost us more to insure our cars if we don’t have a Florida License and also causes problems when using checks in stores without valid ID.

 

I hope that you will look closely at the facts that I have provided. I am a member of our local sub-division’s web-site where most of us short-term rental owners share information and can assure you that many owners have become very unhappy to the extent that several have already put their homes on the market. I may say that they are attempting to ensure that they are purchased by local residents rather than short-term rental owners as they feel that they do not want to be seen to be putting any more money into the tourist trade in Florida. I find this very upsetting and I am sure that you too will feel that this is not what Florida wants. But what are you doing about it? Do you want tourists or is America just shutting its doors to tourists. That is certainly what many of are beginning to feel. I hope that this is not what you want and I am pretty sure it isn’t but it is what us so called ‘Aliens’ are feeling right now.

 

I have relatives who have been in the US since the General Strike in Britain in 1926 and they were made welcome in the ‘land of the free’ it is a pity if that was not still the way America wants it to be. 

 

I may say that many of my American friends fully agree with me and say that they are ashamed of the way their country is treating us, as they say, ‘particularly our friends in the UK.’

 

I look forward to hearing your views on this email and would be very glad to meet with you and discuss my feelings if that was at all possible. Or perhaps the local Senator for our area of Florida would like to meet with us. I could probably arrange for several other owners in our area to meet with him or her. We will be in Florida between November 1st and December 13th of this year.

 

Yours faithfully,

 

Andrena Crawford

From: "Governor Jeb Bush" <jeb.bush@myflorida.com>

Date: Sun, 1 Oct 2006 08:44:14 -0400
For those E-Newsletter recipients who have Adobe Acrobat reader, Governor
Bush's e-newsletter is available in .PDF format by clicking here:

http://www.flgov.com/in_the_news

The text version of the e-newsletter is below.


FAMILY DAY HOSTED AT THE CAPITOL

On Monday, First Lady Columba Bush, Lt. Governor Toni Jennings, and Florida
Office of Drug Control Director Bill Janes and I hosted "Family Day" at the
Capitol to encourage families to spend time together. The celebration
demonstrates how simple activities, such as eating dinner together as a
family, can open the lines of communication, strengthen families and
increase the likelihood children will remain drug-free. Taking an active
role in our children's lives is the single best way to prevent drug use.
Regular conversations and open dialogues are easy ways for parents to learn
more about their children, get to know their friends and help them with the
challenges of growing up in today's world. "Family Day - A Day to Eat
Dinner With Your Children" is part of a national campaign led by President
George W. Bush and the National Center on Addiction and Substance Abuse at
Columbia University (CASA). Families are encouraged to talk to their
children about avoiding the dangers of substance abuse, underage drinking
and smoking. Florida was the first state to adopt the "Family Day" program
in 2001 when President Bush proclaimed it as "a day to spend quality time
with family members and engage in other wholesome activities that help unite
and strengthen the bonds between parents and children". For more
information on "Family Day", please visit www.floridafamilyday.com.


TORREY PINES WELCOMED TO FLORIDA

On Tuesday, I joined Torrey Pines Institute for Molecular Studies Founder
and President Dr. Richard Houghten, incoming Senate President Ken Pruitt and
a host of industry, state and community leaders to officially announce the
Institute's plans to establish a Florida headquarters in the master-planned
community of Tradition in St. Lucie County. The Institute will spur the
creation of many new, high-wage jobs on the Treasure Coast in its pursuit of
significant biomedical research. The decision by Torrey Pines Institute for
Molecular Studies to expand into Florida further establishes our state as a
hub for advanced biomedical research and commercialization. This move will
have a significant impact on the local economy while continuing to build
upon a growing life sciences sector in Florida. I congratulate St. Lucie
and the entire Treasure Coast region for their aggressive and successful
recruitment of Torrey Pines. I wish Torrey Pines great success in Florida.
For more information on my economic development initiatives, please visit
www.myflorida.com.


STUDENTS ATTEMPT TO BREAK A WORLD RECORD

On Thursday, I joined nearly 300,000 middle school students statewide in an
attempt to break the Guinness World Record(tm) for the "Most People Reading
Aloud Simultaneously in Multiple Locations". The event, Breaking a World
Record: Reading Aloud!, aimed to bolster reading among middle school
students. The record attempt was aired via a live public broadcast and
Webcast from Disney-MGM Studios. Promptly at 11:25 a.m., I led the students
in reading an excerpt from the book "Peter and the Starcatchers" written by
Dave Barry and Ridley Pearson. According to Guinness World Records(tm), the
current record is 155,528 students from 737 schools throughout the United
Kingdom who read William Wordsworth's poem "Daffodils", on March 19, 2004.
Jane Feber, an eighth grade teacher from Mandarin Middle School in Duval
County, came up with the idea of breaking the record and shared it with me.
In the coming months, the state will receive confirmation from Guinness as
to whether or not the attempt was successful. To view the Webcast of the
event, please visit www.JustReadFlorida.com.

TIME SENSITIVE MATERIAL

A facsimile from

 

Bryan M. Wohlust
728 Fernwood Drive
West Palm Beach, FL 33405
561-351-8649

To: FEMA APPEALS OFFICER

Fax number: 800-827-8112

Date: 2/9/2006

Regarding: Application No. [REDACTED]   Disaster No. 1609

Comments: 
I just received a notice from your office today and was shocked to see that our request for assistance had been denied stating that “according to a review of your insurance documents, your losses are less than your deductible”.  After reading this,  I am left wondering if the 6 communications with your office have been inaccurate and misleading or if this one letter is inaccurate.

The electric meter and weather pole for the electric for our home were damaged by a tree that fell during Hurricane Wilma.  Florida Power and Light told us we had to have the units replaced before they would restore our power.  We contacted your agency immediately after meeting with an FP&L representative.   We did not get a generator to power our house, or purchase a chain saw to cut the tree (which WOULD have easily been covered by FEMA), we simply used a hand saw and got the permanent power that was damaged beyond repair and that we absolutely needed instead of using the ‘luxury items’ that we could have had covered like a chain saw and temporary power.  My wife, who has a neuro-muscular disease would have benefited from both, but we do not believe in taking advantage of programs that should be used for necessity.

I will review each contact we had with your office and would like a response in the form of an actual letter  - not a form letter -  to advise which communication was correct and why we received such confusing and contradictory information.  

Contact 1: 
When we first contacted FEMA after Hurricane Wilma, my wife spoke with a representative and told her that we did have insurance, however the damage amount was less than our deductible, but still significant enough so that we could not pay for the damage.   We simply do not have access to an unexpected $1300, especially not after paying for expenses preparing for a hurricane and for expenses after in relation to food, yard clean-up, etc.  – and unfortunately we are not in a position where we can take out loans.  As you should know, Floridians can not get insurance deductibles lower than a set percentage of the cost of the home for windstorm damage – there is no alternative.  If we could have a reduced deductible, we probably would.    Regardless, the person she spoke with said that she would list us as uninsured because technically, we did not have coverage for the loss.  

Contact 2:
We then received a denial letter stating that we were denied because we have insurance.

Contact 3:
My wife called the helpline number and spoke with a representative, explaining that yes, we have insurance as she reported but that the 1st representative said that basically we would be considered uninsured because we did not have coverage for the loss so she was listing us as not having insurance.  The new representative said the representative listed us as insured and we had to file an insurance claim.   My wife explained that we were hesitant to file a claim because the loss would not be covered because it was below our deductible and then our insurance rates would go up or we could potentially get dropped from insurance.  Though we know this is not SUPPOSED to happen, we all live in the real world and they DO find a way to drop you or increase rates, regardless of the laws that are SUPPOSED to protect us.   She asked the agent if she could just send our declaration page of the insurance and a copy of the invoice for work to show that the work cost was below our deductible.  The new representative said that it would make sense to do that and gave the FEMA fax number.

Contact 4:
After almost 4 weeks, my wife received a call at work from a FEMA representative stating that she would have to file a claim with the insurance company even though the declaration page showed the loss was less than the deductible.   My wife explained the insurance situation again and the representative stated that the insurance company could not increase our rates for hurricane damage and that we must file a claim and then send FEMA the denial letter in order to be considered for assistance.

Contact 5:
Several days later we received a confusing form letter from FEMA stating that we needed to file a claim with the insurance company but then giving us contradictory direction as to what we needed in regards to documentation for damage.   It also stated we had 10 days from the date on the letter to respond or the application would not be considered (keep in mind it took about 3 days for the letter to get to us, so the clock was ticking, luckily, our insurance company was fast).  We sent all the information that would cover BOTH of the directions on the confusing letter, along with a denial of coverage from our insurance company.   The denial of course, was because the loss was less than our deductible – which my wife said over and over again EVERY time she spoke with a FEMA representative and in every written correspondence.

Contact 6:
Approximately one week after we sent in the denial letter and requested information, we received a call from a FEMA representative that said someone would be coming by to check the damage. Subject:	Flood Insurance Crisis - We need your help
Attachments:	Press Release.doc

As residents of Destin, Florida, we desperately need your help with our flood insurance crisis.
 
We, like over two thousand other homeowners in our area, have recently learned that we cannot obtain flood insurance because our homes are within a CBRA zone.  We are ineligible for coverage under the National Flood Insurance Program which prohibits federal assistance to Coastal Barrier Resource Areas, and we have found that we cannot buy insurance in the private sector because they are no longer writing flood insurance policies in CBRA zones.
 
Until a few months ago, we were able to obtain coverage through private insurers.  Without this protection we now find ourselves totally vulnerable to the threat of a major storm.  Not only do we face the possibility of losing our life's major investment but also the inability to sell our "uninsurable" home except to someone who can buy it without a mortgage (since lenders require flood insurance in a SFHA) and who is willing to forego flood insurance coverage.
 
This dilemma has had a major impact on the real estate market in our community.  Sales are at a dead standstill, and property values are dropping dramatically.  As you must realize, this ultimately will result in the loss of local economic health.  In August Governor Bush appointed a new "Committee for a Sustainable Emerald Coast" to chart the course for the future of our region.  A solution to our flood insurance crisis is critical to sustaining the economy of the Emerald Coast!
 
Attached is a full description of this issue, as well as possible remedies, written by Robert Guidara, who is a member of the Taskforce for Attainable Flood Insurance (TAFI).  We are asking that you please read this material and do what you can to help restore a readily available and reasonably affordable way to obtain flood insurance.
 
Steve and Kay Bonn
Destin, Florida

Profera, a personal friend, colleague and former classmate from The Ohio College of Podiatric Medicine and acting Chief of the Salem Virginia Veterans Administration Hospital Podiatric Department, regarding an application for the RPR 12 Podiatric Residency Program offered in July of 1997. Dr. Haritatos (Semko's) intent was to gain hospital experience and exposure to veteran related Podiatric problems. In May of 1997, Dr. Haritaos (Semko) accompanied by her partner and husband, Dr. Daniel Semko, traveled to Salem, Virginia to visit their old friend and learn about the residency program. During that period of investigation, both Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko learned that Dr. Profera was involved in a bitter divorce and in difficult financial straights. Dr. Semko, as a friend, offered to loan Dr. Profera funds to assist with his financial difficulties. After this visit, upon returning to their active practice in Richmond, Indiana, and upon consideration of the program and the logistics of their clinical practice, Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko concluded that a full time position for Dr. Haritatos (Semko) at the Residency program in Salem, Virginia, could be arranged provided that Dr. Semko assumed and was able to continue on his own, the full responsibilities of their joint practice. When this information was conveyed to Dr. Profera, he stated that since he had two positions to fill and because Drs. Haritatos (Semko) and Semko were married, he wanted both doctors to accept the open billets. Dr. Profera stated that he had complete discretion over the program and could modify the programs such that their Indiana Podiatric practice would not be jeopardized. Accordingly, Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko agreed to accept the positions commencing July 1, 1997. In October of 1997, both Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko became increasingly ware that Dr. Profera was not providing the scheduled hospital rotations previously promised as being included in the residency program. Attempts to have access to these rotations severely enhanced Dr. Profera's agitation which appeared chronically maximized by his impending divorce and other reasons unrelated to the residency program. In late January to early February, the situation deteriorated significantly. In early February of 1998, Dr. Profera was repeatedly irrational and abusive to Dr. Haritatos (Semko). As a result, Dr. Semko, who was for the most part maintaining their clinical practice in Richmond, Indiana, felt that protective actions for his wife's interests and safety were necessary. Without warning, Dr. Profera then announced the termination of the program to Dr. Haritatos (Semko). Dr. Semko arrived in Salem to assist his wife in leaving the program shortly thereafter. During the process of terminating their V.A. authorizations, Dr. Semko and Dr. Haritatos (Semko) learned that Dr. Profera in fact did not have the authority to modify or terminate the residency program. Dr. Profera had approached the Chief of Staff stating that although he had stated that he was terminating the program, he wanted both doctors to receive "certificates of completion" which was indeed a break from the accepted standards which governed the residency program. That same day, Dr. Profera approached the hospital security chief and stated that he "thought that he was in the middle of a bribery scheme." These conflicting actions initiated an FBI investigation regarding the entire situation. In June of 2002, Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko fully cooperated with the federal government's investigation and prosecution. Each provided a statement to the government that the above referenced funds had been lent to Dr. Profera in part to assist him but as well with the goal of achieving preferential treatment for Dr. Semko in regard to the relaxation of the requirement of Dr. Semko's physical presence at the Salem V.A. residency program. Further, Dr. Semko and Dr. Haritatos(Semko) indicated that checks were automatically deposited and transferred for Dr. Semko's services to the V.A. residency. Page Two Dr. Haritatos (Semko) plead guilty to aiding and abetting misdemeanor theft which stemmed from the cashing of the V.A. check in the amount of $802.00 pursuant to her husband Dr. Semko's services to the residency which the government alleged Dr. Semko had not fully performed. Dr. Semko plead guilty to one count of wire fraud which stemmed from the wiring of funds for a paycheck issued to Dr. Semko which had been automatically deposited into the V.A. Credit Union and then check transferred to the Semko's checking account in Richmond, Indiana. The court ordered and Drs. Semko and Dr. Haritatos (Semko), paid complete restitution of funds derived from Dr. Semko's salary. Additionally, the court imposed a fine against each doctor and placed each on probation Dr. Semko and Dr. Haritatos (Semko) have taken full and complete responsibility for their actions none of which are remotely related to their Podiatric practice. Prior to this incident, both doctors have maintained careers of gainful employment in private practice, have had no civil, criminal or medical infractions and have provided a valuable service to the residents of Richmond. The sole purpose of exploring the V.A. Residency Program was to enhance Dr. Haritatos (Semko's) hospital and veteran exposure. Dr. Semko has an extensive medical background as a Navy Hospital Corpsman stationed in Viet Nam and as an Orthopedic Physicians Assistant. His personal benefit from the V.A. program other than supporting his wife's desire to expand her medical experience, would have been negligible at best. Dr. Semko and Dr. Haritatos (Semko) consider this bizarre series of circumstances to be an aberration. Each doctor has made complete financial restitution and abided by the probationary guidelines set forth by the court. Both doctors satisfied all of the requirements, fines and guidelines set forth by the court and were duly released from all encumbrances. Dr. Haritatos (Semko) and Dr. Semko deeply regret the difficulties and inconveniences resulting from this matter.

Dear Governor Bush, 

In February 2006, I wrote to you requesting your assistance with my retirement from the United States Secret Service. I followed your advice and the results were very informative.

On June 20, 2006, I received a response from Senator Kennedy concerning an inquiry he made on my behalf to the U.S. Department of Homeland Security - U. S. Secret Service.

I was happy to learn I had to appeal a decision made by the Merit Systems Protection Board (MSPB). The Initial Decision was rendered in April 2000, termination, by Judge William C. Jenkins. I never received the Initial Decision, which gave me the opportunity to appeal within 30 days. I spoke with Bernard Parker, a clerk with the MSPB, he stated to file an appeal, but the length of time was a concern to him. I wrote a letter to the Clerk of the Board, Mr. Roberts, to request an extension of time to file for a petition for review. He has denied my request to file a petition for review. As stated earlier, I never received the initial decision, and was made aware of it, through the research Senator Kennedy asked the Secret Service to initiate.

I brought a lawsuit against the Secret Service for discrimination, in 1996. I won, and then retaliation began. My family was affected and my marriage deteriorated. Allegations were made by my husband, and brought to the attention of Inspector Teter, who was named in the initial lawsuit, who came to my home and confiscated our antique gun collection, which was packaged and stored in the attic of our residence. He then had my gun and badge removed. All this was done without my being questioned about my husbands allegations, or any investigation ever being conducted by Inspector Teter. 

Because of the harrassment, we agreed to retire at 66 2/3. My concern was that the attorney never addressed the first lawsuit; therefore, the retaliation was never addressed. I ran out of money paying both my divorce attorney and work attorney. 

I took the tests required by the Secret Service Police and Fire Clinic, to go before the retirement board. I learned the Secret Service doctors had diagnosed depression, without ever having seen me. The diagnose was not from the Police and Fire Clinic, but from an outside doctor, hired by the Secret Service. After taking the test, I began to have second thoughts about retiring, without legal representation, to address the depression issue, because, I did not feel depressed. I asked the doctor, who administered the test for retirement, if I could finish with my divorce first. I would then retain an attorney for my retirement. The Police and Fire Clinic doctor agreed.

I was contacted by Saic Buck Tanis, who was not familiar with me or my case, gave me an ultimatum to either resign or be terminated. The hearing was held with the DC Merit Protection Board, whose decision I had not received until Senator Kennedy’s assistance, in June 2006. 

The reason for my agreement to retire was the retaliation I received. There was no disciplinary action, or any wrongdoing on my part. My yearly evaluations were above average. None of these things played a part in MSPB Judge Jenkins decision to accept termination. The reason I was terminated was due to the expiration of my top-secret clearance, which is explained in the attached letter.

I would like to appeal, Judge Jenkins decision, and have the termination removed from my record and my Top Secret Security Clearance returned. I had a 20-year retirement under the DC Police and Firemans Retirement System. The U.S. Secret Service hired me in 1981, I would have retired in 2001, and I was terminated in 2000, with 19 years on. 

PLEASE, assist me with my retirement. I have three children who are in high school and will be going to college. With termination on my record, it is extremely difficult to get any where near the salary of $54,000.00, which I made with the U.S. Secret Service. Financially, I fear for our future.

I have hired the law firm of Mahoney & Mahoney, 1300 Penn. Ave Wash., D.C. (202) 204-2520. I have sent them a $7,500.00 retainer, which I got, from taking out my retirement deductions from the Police and Fire Retirement Board. The attorney’s have indicated that retirement looks bleak, because, the Secret Service has won. It would not benefit them to give me my retirement. I do not consider this a win, lose competition. I would like to receive what is rightfully mine, and was unable to attain because I did not receive the initial decision given by the DC Merit Protection Board.

Would it be possible for you to ask your brother, the President, and your Mom and Dad, to request Secret Service Director Sullivan to assist me with my retirement process, to have the termination reversed through Secret Service Counsel, my Top Secret Clearance reinstated, and pursue my retirement as we all initially agreed, or a reinstatement to finish my retirement, so I can count on a fairly, financially secure future for myself and my children.

Thank you so much for all of your assistance.

Sincerely,

Linda Jwanouskos

From:	scottwtolbert@aol.com
Sent:	Sunday, October 1, 2006 2:08 PM
To:	Governor Jeb Bush
Cc:	jarrizurieta@floridaftaa.org; abecker@becker-poliakoff.com; t.david@alliance-companies.com; cfacs@gate.net; ppizarro@us.telefonica.com; JLedlow@acarra.com; scottwtolbert@aol.com
Subject:	Immigration and Jobs for America - a Joint Development process

Honorable Governor,
 
I have been working in Great State of Florida for over 17 years; have graduated from several of our highly esteemed State of Florida Universities (FSU, FAU) and the University of Miami (MBA International Business). I have worked with many Fortune 500 companies in providing consultation services in the area of Contact Centers - Office Depot, IBM, GTECH, Spirit Airlines, Ocwen, Assurant, TracFone, and State of Florida Technology Office.  A trend of major concern has been taking place over the past few years to off shore contact center agents to the Philippines, India, South America and other foreign countries due the inherently cheaper labor costs.  This trend represents a sound business decision by the owners of these enterprises given the current costs of labor, government incentives, laws and the advent of newer and cheaper transport technologies.
 
Undoubtedly, this trend started many years prior to 2000 as these countries have been re-tooling their workers to become knowledge workers. The skills of English Language, Computer Literacy, and Cultural Training are not learned over night, they are results of pro-active attempts by competing governments to seize an economic strong hold to employ their workers. Examples of Tax Benefits, waived Import Duties etc are all part of these governments war chest on the Economics of employing their constituents. 
 
As a technologist with ambitions to serve my community, I met you briefly at the Miami Seaport as part of the DR-CAFTA discussions where you had the honor of hosting three presidents from South & Central America. Our friend, Jorge Arrizurieta was also a key speaker at the Biltmore. Key to their lectures was joint economic prosperity. 
 
Currently, technology exists, and is exploited, to allow off shoring and near shoring of Contact Center Agents - robbing the economic benefit to the local U.S. economies. Major organizations utilize this technology to employ two to three thousand agents per company outside of U.S Governments jurisdiction, taxes and regulations. Under a level playing field, I am typically opposed to government interference and support a laissez-faire state of affairs. I can however argue that the situation is not fair due to outside influences of Government incentives and that the foundation of the U.S. Service Economy is at jeopardy. It is at jeopardy as consumers no longer visit businesses face to face but conducts transactions via the telephone, Internet, email and Interactive Voice Response systems. And as such, these services have shifted to off shore locations in major proportions. The U.S used to be an industrial nation but we gave this leadership to China and Japan and moved to the Service Economy model. Although this is part of the natural order of economic theory, I am not quite sure how we intend to grow this segment if the services are in fact supplied outside of the U.S. What I do see is an economic windfall for competing governments and more and more U.S. Workers being displaced.
 
I offer a solution that is both fair and reciprocal in nature and that I bequest to get your thoughts and support to begin an endeavor that brings the end result of Economic Prosperity and cultural exchange to participating governments. I have simplified my thoughts in the following paragraph as a starting point in dialogue with you and other U.S. leaders and to gain your support of such a solution. After more meaningful discussions we could more clearly define this strategy to one that is both acceptable and embraced by policy makers in the U.S and your constituents.  
 
The main principle behind the program is to bring foreign workers to the U.S to curtail the contact center gold rush on foreign soil. Bringing these workers to U.S Shores in a temporary fashion for Training, Employment and Worker exchange would have multiple effects on the economic prosperity of both nations. The program could be structured such that in exchange for financial incentives via public and private sources, a percentage of the total contact center work force would have to be U.S Based (preferably Florida). Further more a sub set of these workers in the US would in fact be also required to be from the foreign countries. Work Permits would be given to these companies for a fixed term limit that would bring workers to the U.S. to work at wages commensurable with US Wages. This would allow the workers to learn U.S Culture, be taxed by U.S and provide economic growth at the local areas. US workers would naturally rise to positions of leaderships within the U.S. based contact center due to longevity and the Foreign workers would benefit economically, intellectually and culturally.
 
I think that some of the same issues we face with our current H-1B, H-1B1, or E-3 and the proposed guest worker program would be challenged with this program. However, due to a solid reciprocal economic approach, we would perhaps gain support on both sides do the fence and would in fact be an impetus for Presidents Bush Guest Worker Program.
 
Alexander the Great, King of Macedon understood the "policy of fusion" in building his empire. As a cause and effect reaction, U.S Relations with participating governments would steadily establish stronger bonds. Foreign workers would become spokesman for U.S labor practices and ideas of democracy and freedom would ring prominently through out the world. An epidemic of prosperity could be started that is supportive of joint economic prosperity.
 
Although I have over simplified the idea to keep this note short and to the point, I would like to spend some time with you and others to discuss your thoughts and to begin to rally support for such a program. Please provide me some time on your calendar. I am available at your command.
 
 
 
"All great questions of politics and economics come down in the last analysis to the decisions and actions of individual men and women. They are questions of human relations, and we ought always to think about them in terms of men and women-the individual human beings who are involved in them. If we can get human relations on a proper basis, the statistics, finance and all other complicated technical aspects of these questions will be easier to solve."
- Thomas J. Watson (1874-1956)
Founder, chairman & president of IBM
 
With Highest Regards:
 
Scott Walter Tolbert
